{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01DwKtSWhNgVCgbmNi7HUkqX","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→/*\n     2→Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n     3→\n     4→Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n     5→you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n     6→You may obtain a copy of the License at\n     7→\n     8→    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n     9→\n    10→Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n    11→distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n    12→WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n    13→See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n    14→limitations under the License.\n    15→*/\n    16→\n    17→package cache\n    18→\n    19→import (\n    20→\t\"context\"\n    21→\t\"errors\"\n    22→\t\"fmt\"\n    23→\t\"sync\"\n    24→\t\"sync/atomic\"\n    25→\t\"time\"\n    26→\n    27→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\"\n    28→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\"\n    29→\tutilruntime \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n    30→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n    31→\t\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/synctrack\"\n    32→\t\"k8s.io/utils/buffer\"\n    33→\t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n    34→\t\"k8s.io/utils/ptr\"\n    35→\n    36→\t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n    37→\n    38→\tclientgofeaturegate \"k8s.io/client-go/features\"\n    39→)\n    40→\n    41→// SharedInformer provides eventually consistent linkage of its\n    42→// clients to the authoritative state of a given collection of\n    43→// objects.  An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n    44→// namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n    45→// an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n    46→// SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n    47→// group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n    48→// SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n    49→// applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n    50→//\n    51→// The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n    52→// access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n    53→// An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n    54→// other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n    55→//\n    56→// A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n    57→// by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n    58→// machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n    59→// the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n    60→// consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n    61→// prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n    62→// particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n    63→// then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n    64→// eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n    65→// state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n    66→// service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n    67→// absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n    68→// selector.\n    69→//\n    70→// For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n    71→// states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n    72→// states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n    73→// might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n    74→// states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n    75→// ordering between states seen for different objects.\n    76→//\n    77→// The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n    78→// during `Run()`.\n    79→//\n    80→// As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n    81→// unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n    82→// collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n    83→// SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n    84→// collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n    85→// service ends, or communication problems between the two\n    86→// persistently thwart achievement).\n    87→//\n    88→// As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n    89→// non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n    90→// removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n    91→// removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n    92→// too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n    93→// problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n    94→//\n    95→// The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n    96→// objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n    97→// Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n    98→// a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n    99→// into its constituent parts.\n   100→//\n   101→// Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n   102→// snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n   103→// will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n   104→//\n   105→// A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n   106→// update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n   107→// added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n   108→// stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n   109→// after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n   110→// additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n   111→// client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n   112→// local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n   113→// SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n   114→// update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n   115→// update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n   116→// corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n   117→// and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n   118→// For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n   119→// delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n   120→// object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n   121→// `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n   122→// that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n   123→// `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n   124→// and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n   125→// created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n   126→// rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n   127→// need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n   128→// field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n   129→// notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n   130→//\n   131→// A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n   132→// is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n   133→// notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n   134→// to something else, for example through a\n   135→// `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n   136→//\n   137→// A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n   138→// state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n   139→// ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\n   140→type SharedInformer interface {\n   141→\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n   142→\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n   143→\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n   144→\t// different handlers.\n   145→\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n   146→\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n   147→\t// seen every item in the initial list).\n   148→\t//\n   149→\t// Contextual logging: AddEventHandlerWithOptions together with a logger in the options should be used instead of AddEventHandler in code which supports contextual logging.\n   150→\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n// namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n// an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n// SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n// group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n// SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n// applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n//\n// The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n// access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n// An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n// other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n//\n// A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n// by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n// machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n// the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n// consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n// prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n// particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n// then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n// eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n// state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n// service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n// absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n// selector.\n//\n// For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n// states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n// states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n// might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n// states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n// ordering between states seen for different objects.\n//\n// The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n// during `Run()`.\n//\n// As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n// unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n// collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n// SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n// collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n// service ends, or communication problems between the two\n// persistently thwart achievement).\n//\n// As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n// non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n// removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n// removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n// too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n// problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n//\n// The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n// objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n// Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n// a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n// into its constituent parts.\n//\n// Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n// snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n// will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n//\n// A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n// update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n// added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n// stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n// after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n// additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n// client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n// local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n// SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n// update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n// update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n// corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n// and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n// For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n// delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n// object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n// `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n// that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n// `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n// and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n// created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n// rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n// need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n// field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n// notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n//\n// A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n// is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n// notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n// to something else, for example through a\n// `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n//\n// A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n// state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n// ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\ntype SharedInformer interface {\n\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n\t// different handlers.\n\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n\t// seen every item in the initial list).\n\t//\n\t// Contextual logging: AddEventHandlerWithOptions together with a logger in the options should be used instead of AddEventHandler in code which supports contextual logging.\n\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1144}}}

  203→// Returns true once this controller has completed an initial resource listing\n   204→func (c *controller) HasSynced() bool {\n   205→\treturn c.config.Queue.HasSynced()\n   206→}\n   207→\n This will require a little thought\n   219→// to make sure that we don't end up processing the same object multiple times\n   220→// concurrently.\n   221→func (c *controller) processLoop(ctx context.Context) {\n   222→\tuseBatchProcess := false\n   223→\tbatchQueue, ok := c.config.Queue.(QueueWithBatch)\n   224→\tif ok && c.config.ProcessBatch != nil && clientgofeaturegate.FeatureGates().Enabled(clientgofeaturegate.InOrderInformersBatchProcess) {\n   225→\t\tuseBatchProcess = true\n   226→\t}\n   227→\tfor {\n   228→\t\tselect {\n   229→\t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n   230→\t\t\treturn\n   231→\t\tdefault:\n   232→\t\t\tvar err error\n   233→\t\t\tif useBatchProcess {\n   234→\t\t\t\terr = batchQueue.PopBatch(c.config.ProcessBatch, PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\n   235→\t\t\t} else {\n   236→\t\t\t\t// otherwise fallback to non-batch process behavior\n   237→\t\t\t\t_, err = c.config.Pop(PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\n   238→\t\t\t}\n   239→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   240→\t\t\t\tif errors.Is(err, ErrFIFOClosed) {\n   241→\t\t\t\t\treturn\n   242→\t\t\t\t}\n   243→\t\t\t}\n   244→\t\t}\n   245→\t}\n   246→}\n   247→\n   248→// ResourceEventHandler can handle notifications for events that\n   249→// happen to a resource. The events are informational only, so you\n   250→// can't return an error.  The handlers MUST NOT modify the objects\n   251→// received; this concerns not only the top level of structure but all\n   252→// the data structures reachable from it.\n   253→//   - OnAdd is called when an object is added.\n   254→//   - OnUpdate is called when an object is modified. Note that oldObj is the\n   255→//     last known state of the object-- it is possible that several changes\n   256→//     were combined together, so you can't use this to see every single\n   257→//     change. OnUpdate is also called when a re-list happens, and it will\n   258→//     get called even if nothing changed. This is useful for periodically\n   259→//     evaluating or syncing something.\n   260→//   - OnDelete will get the final state of the item if it is known, otherwise\n   261→//     it will get an object of type DeletedFinalStateUnknown. This can\n   262→//     happen if the watch is closed and misses the delete event and we don't\n   263→//     notice the deletion until the subsequent re-list.\n   264→type ResourceEventHandler interface {\n   265→\tOnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\n   266→\tOnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n   267→\tOnDelete(obj interface{})\n   268→}\n   269→\n   270→// ResourceEventHandlerFuncs is an adaptor to let you easily specify as many or\n   271→// as few of the notification functions as you want while still implementing\n   272→// ResourceEventHandler.   317→\t}\n   318→}\n   319→\n   320→// OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\n   321→func (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n   322→\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\n   323→\t\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\n   324→\t}\n   325→}\n   326→\n   327→// OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\n   328→func (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n   329→\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\n   330→\t\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\n   331→\t}\n   332→}\n   333→\n   334→// FilteringResourceEventHandler applies the provided filter to all events coming\n   335→// in, ensuring the appropriate nested handler method is invoked. An object\n   336→// that starts passing the filter after an update is considered an add, and an\n   337→// object that stops passing the filter after an update is considered a delete.\n   338→// Like the handlers, the filter MUST NOT modify the objects it is given.\n   339→type FilteringResourceEventHandler struct {\n   340→\tFilterFunc func(obj interface{}) bool\n   341→\tHandler    ResourceEventHandler\n   342→}\n   343→\n   344→// OnAdd calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\n   345→func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n   346→\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n   347→\t\treturn\n   348→\t}\n   349→\tr.Handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n   350→}\n   351→\n   352→// OnUpdate ensures the proper handler is called depending on whether the filter matches\n   353→func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n   354→\tnewer := r.FilterFunc(newObj)\n   355→\tolder := r.FilterFunc(oldObj)\n   356→\tswitch {\n   357→\tcase newer && older:\n   358→\t\tr.Handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\n   359→\tcase newer && !older:\n   360→\t\tr.Handler.OnAdd(newObj, false)\n   361→\tcase !newer && older:\n   362→\t\tr.Handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\n   363→\tdefault:\n   364→\t\t// do nothing\n   365→\t}\n   366→}\n   367→\n   368→// OnDelete calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\n   369→func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n   370→\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n   371→\t\treturn\n   372→\t}\n   373→\tr.Handler.OnDelete(obj)\n   374→}\n   375→\n   376→// DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc checks for\n   377→// DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n   378→// MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\n   379→func DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj interface{}) (string, error) {\n   380→\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n   381→\t\treturn d.Key, nil\n   382→\t}\n   383→\treturn MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n   384→}\n   385→\n   386→// DeletionHandlingObjectToName checks for\n   387→// DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n   388→// ObjectToName.\n   389→func DeletionHandlingObjectToName(obj interface{}) (ObjectName, error) {\n   390→\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n   391→\t\treturn ParseObjectName(d.Key)\n   392→\t}\n   393→\treturn ObjectToName(obj)\n   394→}\n   395→\n   396→// InformerOptions configure a Reflector.\n   397→type InformerOptions struct {\n   398→\t// ListerWatcher implements List and Watch functions for the source of the resource\n   399→\t// the informer will be informing about.\n   400→\tListerWatcher ListerWatcher\n   401→\n   402→\t// ObjectType is an object of the type that informer is expected to receive.\n   403→\tObjectType runtime.Object\n   404→\n   405→\t// Handler defines functions that should called on object mutations.\n   406→\tHandler ResourceEventHandler\n   407→\n   408→\t// ResyncPeriod is the underlying Reflector's resync period. If non-zero, the store\n   409→\t// is re-synced with that frequency - Modify events are delivered even if objects\n   410→\t// didn't change.\n   411→\t// This is useful for synchronizing objects that configure external resources\n   412→\t// (e.g. configure cloud provider functionalities).\n   413→\t// Optional - if unset, store resyncing is not happening periodically.\n   414→\tResyncPeriod time.Duration\n   415→\n   416→\t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\n   417→\t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\n   418→\t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\n   419→\t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\n   420→\tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\n   421→\n   422→\t// Indexers, if set, are the indexers for the received objects to optimize\n   423→\t// certain queries.\n   424→\t// Optional - if unset no indexes are maintained.\n   425→\tIndexers Indexers\n   426→\n   427→\t// Transform function, if set, will be called on all objects before they will be\n   428→\t// put into the Store and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will be invoked\n   429→\t// for them.\n   430→\t// Optional - if unset no additional transforming is happening.\n   431→\tTransform TransformFunc\n   432→}\n   433→\n   434→// NewInformerWithOptions returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\n   435→// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n   436→// Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n   437→// notifications to be faulty.\n   438→func NewInformerWithOptions(options InformerOptions) (Store, Controller) {\n   439→\tvar clientState Store\n   440→\tif options.Indexers == nil {\n   441→\t\tclientState = NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n   442→\t} else {\n   443→\t\tclientState = NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, options.Indexers)\n   444→\t}\n   445→\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n   446→}\n   447→\n   448→// NewInformer returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\n   449→// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n   450→// Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n   451→// notifications to be faulty.\n   452→//\n   453→// Parameters:\n   454→//   - lw is list and watch functions for the source of the resource you want to\n   455→//     be informed of.\n   456→//   - objType is an object of the type that you expect to receive.\n   457→//   - resyncPeriod: if non-zero, will re-list this often (you will get OnUpdate\n   458→//     calls, even if nothing changed). Otherwise, re-list will be delayed as\n   459→//     long as possible (until the upstream source closes the watch or times out,\n   460→//     or you stop the controller).\n   461→//   - h is the object you want notifications sent to.\n   462→//\n   463→// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\n   464→func NewInformer(\n   465→\tlw ListerWatcher,\n   466→\tobjType runtime.Object,\n   467→\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n   468→\th ResourceEventHandler,\n   469→) (Store, Controller) {\n   470→\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n   471→\tclientState := NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n   472→\n   473→\toptions := InformerOptions{\n   474→\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n   475→\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n   476→\t\tHandler:       h,\n   477→\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n   478→\t}\n   479→\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n   480→}\n   481→\n   482→// NewIndexerInformer returns an Indexer and a Controller for populating the index\n   483→// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n   484→// Index for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n   485→// notifications to be faulty.\n   486→//\n   487→// Parameters:\n   488→//   - lw is list and watch functions for the source of the resource you want to\n   489→//     be informed of.\n   490→//   - objType is an object of the type that you expect to receive.\n   491→//   - resyncPeriod: if non-zero, will re-list this often (you will get OnUpdate\n   492→//     calls, even if nothing changed). You should only used\n   521→// the returned Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause\n   522→// the event notifications to be faulty.\n   523→// The given transform function will be called on all objects before they will\n   524→// put into the Store and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will\n   525→// be invoked for them.\n   526→//\n   527→// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\n   528→func NewTransformingInformer(\n   529→\tlw ListerWatcher,\n   530→\tobjType runtime.Object,\n   531→\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n   532→\th ResourceEventHandler,\n   533→\ttransformer TransformFunc,\n   534→) (Store, Controller) {\n   535→\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n   536→\tclientState := NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n   537→\n   538→\toptions := InformerOptions{\n   539→\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n   540→\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n   541→\t\tHandler:       h,\n   542→\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n   543→\t\tTransform:     transformer,\n   544→\t}\n   545→\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n   546→}\n   547→\n   548→// NewTransformingIndexerInformer returns an Indexer and a controller for\n   549→// populating the index while also providing event notifications. You should\n   550→// only used the returned Index for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes\n   551→// will cause the event notifications to be faulty.\n   552→// The given transform function will be called on all objects before they will\n   553→// be put into the Index and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will\n   554→// be invoked for them.\n   555→//\n   556→// Deprecated: Use ResourceEventHandler,\n   562→\tindexers Indexers,\n   563→\ttransformer TransformFunc,\n   564→) (Indexer, Controller) {\n   565→\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n   566→\tclientState := NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, indexers)\n   567→\n   568→\toptions := InformerOptions{\n   569→\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n   570→\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n   577→}\n   578→\n   579→// Multiplexes updates in the form of a list of Deltas into a Store, and informs\n   580→// a given handler of events OnUpdate, OnAdd, OnDelete\n   581→func processDeltas(\n   582→\t// Object which receives event notifications from the given deltas\n   583→\thandler ResourceEventHandler,\n   584→\tclientState Store,\n   585→\tdeltas Deltas,\n   586→\tisInInitialList bool,\n   587→\tkeyFunc KeyFunc,\n   588→) error {\n   589→\t// from oldest to newest\n   590→\tfor _, d := range deltas {\n   591→\t\tobj := d.Object\n   592→\n   593→\t\tswitch d.Type {\n   594→\t\tcase ReplacedAll:\n   595→\t\t\tinfo, ok := obj.(ReplacedAllInfo)\n   596→\t\t\tif !ok {\n   597→\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"ReplacedAll did not contain ReplacedAllInfo: %T\", obj)\n   598→\t\t\t}\n   599→\t\t\tif err := processReplacedAllInfo(handler, info, clientState, isInInitialList, keyFunc); err != nil {\n   600→\t\t\t\treturn err\n   601→\t\t\t}\n   602→\t\tcase SyncAll:\n   603→\t\t\t_, ok := obj.(SyncAllInfo)\n   604→\t\t\tif !ok {\n   605→\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"SyncAll did not contain SyncAllInfo: %T\", obj)\n   606→\t\t\t}\n   607→\t\t\tobjs := clientState.List()\n   608→\t\t\tfor _, obj := range objs {\n   609→\t\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(obj, obj)\n   610→\t\t\t}\n   611→\t\t\treturn nil\n   612→\t\tcase Sync, Replaced, Added, Updated:\n   613→\t\t\tif old, exists, err := clientState.Get(obj); err == nil && exists {\n   614→\t\t\t\tif err := clientState.Update(obj); err != nil {\n   615→\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n   616→\t\t\t\t}\n   617→\t\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(old, obj)\n   618→\t\t\t} else {\n   619→\t\t\t\tif err := clientState.Add(obj); err != nil {\n   620→\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n   621→\t\t\t\t}\n   622→\t\t\t\thandler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n   623→\t\t\t}\n   624→\t\tcase Deleted:\n   625→\t\t\tif err := clientState.Delete(obj); err != nil {\n   626→\t\t\t\treturn err\n   627→\t\t\t}\n   628→\t\t\thandler.OnDelete(obj)\n   629→\t\t}\n   630→\t}\n   631→\treturn nil\n   632→}\n   633→\n   634→// processDeltasInBatch applies a batch of Delta objects to the given Store and\n   635→// notifies the ResourceEventHandler of add, update, or delete events.\n   636→//\n   637→// If the Store supports transactions (TransactionStore), all Deltas are applied\n   638→// atomically in a single transaction and corresponding handler callbacks are\n   639→// executed afterward. Otherwise, each Delta is processed individually.\n   640→//\n   641→// Returns an error if any Delta or transaction fails. For TransactionError,\n   642→// only successful operations trigger callbacks.\n   643→func processDeltasInBatch(\n   644→\thandler ResourceEventHandler,\n   645→\tclientState Store,\n   646→\tdeltas []Delta,\n   647→\tisInInitialList bool,\n   648→\tkeyFunc KeyFunc,\n   649→) error {\n   650→\t// from oldest to newest\n   651→\ttxns := make([]Transaction, 0)\n   652→\tcallbacks := make([]func(), 0)\n   653→\ttxnStore, txnSupported := clientState.(TransactionStore)\n   654→\tif !txnSupported {\n   655→\t\tvar errs []error\n   656→\t\tfor _, delta := range deltas {\n   657→\t\t\tif err := processDeltas(handler, clientState, Deltas{delta}, isInInitialList, keyFunc); err != nil {\n   658→\t\t\t\terrs = append(errs, err)\n   659→\t\t\t}\n   660→\t\t}\n   661→\t\tif len(errs) > 0 {\n   662→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected error when handling deltas: %v\", errs)\n   663→\t\t}\n   664→\t\treturn nil\n   665→\t}\n   666→\t// deltasList is a list of unique objects\n   667→\tfor _, d := range deltas {\n   668→\t\tobj := d.Object\n   669→\t\tswitch d.Type {\n   670→\t\tcase Sync, Replaced, Added, Updated:\n   671→\t\t\t// it will only return one old object for each because items are unique\n   672→\t\t\tif old, exists, err := clientState.Get(obj); err == nil && exists {\n   673→\t\t\t\ttxn := Transaction{\n   674→\t\t\t\t\tType:   TransactionTypeUpdate,\n   675→\t\t\t\t\tObject: obj,\n   676→\t\t\t\t}\n   677→\t\t\t\ttxns = append(txns, txn)\n   678→\t\t\t\tcallbacks = append(callbacks, func() {\n   679→\t\t\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(old, obj)\n   680→\t\t\t\t})\n   681→\t\t\t} else {\n   682→\t\t\t\ttxn := Transaction{\n   683→\t\t\t\t\tType:   TransactionTypeAdd,\n   684→\t\t\t\t\tObject: obj,\n   685→\t\t\t\t}\n   686→\t\t\t\ttxns = append(txns, txn)\n   687→\t\t\t\tcallbacks = append(callbacks, func() {\n   688→\t\t\t\t\thandler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n   689→\t\t\t\t})\n   690→\t\t\t}\n   691→\t\tcase Deleted:\n   692→\t\t\ttxn := Transaction{\n   693→\t\t\t\tType:   TransactionTypeDelete,\n   694→\t\t\t\tObject: obj,\n   695→\t\t\t}\n   696→\t\t\ttxns = append(txns, txn)\n   697→\t\t\tcallbacks = append(callbacks, func() {\n   698→\t\t\t\thandler.OnDelete(obj)\n   699→\t\t\t})\n   700→\t\tdefault:\n   701→\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"Delta type %s is not supported in batch processing\", d.Type)\n   702→\t\t}\n   703→\t}\n   704→\n   705→\terr := txnStore.Transaction(txns...)\n   706→\tif err != nil {\n   707→\t\t// if txn had error, only execute the callbacks for the successful ones\n   708→\t\tfor _, i := range err.SuccessfulIndices {\n   709→\t\t\tif i < len(callbacks) {\n   710→\t\t\t\tcallbacks[i]()\n   711→\t\t\t}\n   712→\t\t}\n   713→\t\t// formatting the error so txns doesn't escape and keeps allocated in the stack.\n   714→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"not all items in the batch successfully processed: %s\", err.Error())\n   715→\t}\n   716→\tfor _, callback := range callbacks {\n   717→\t\tcallback()\n   718→\t}\n   719→\treturn nil\n   720→}\n   721→\n   722→func processReplacedAllInfo(handler ResourceEventHandler, info ReplacedAllInfo, clientState Store, isInInitialList bool, keyFunc KeyFunc) error {\n   723→\tvar deletions []DeletedFinalStateUnknown\n   724→\ttype replacement struct {\n   725→\t\toldObj interface{}\n   726→\t\tnewObj interface{}\n   727→\t}\n   728→\treplacements := make([]replacement, 0, len(info.Objects))\n   729→\n   730→\terr := reconcileReplacement(nil, clientState, info.Objects, keyFunc,\n   731→\t\tfunc(obj DeletedFinalStateUnknown) error {\n   732→\t\t\tdeletions = append(deletions, obj)\n   733→\t\t\treturn nil\n   734→\t\t},\n   735→\t\tfunc(obj interface{}) error {\n   736→\t\t\t// This behavior matches processDeltas handling of Replace deltas\n   737→\t\t\tif old, exists, err := clientState.Get(obj); err == nil && exists {\n   738→\t\t\t\treplacements = append(replacements, replacement{newObj: obj, oldObj: old})\n   739→\t\t\t} else {\n   740→\t\t\t\treplacements = append(replacements, replacement{newObj: obj})\n   741→\t\t\t}\n   742→\t\t\treturn nil\n   743→\t\t},\n   744→\t)\n   745→\tif err != nil {\n   746→\t\treturn err\n   747→\t}\n   748→\n   749→\t// Replace the client state first so the store reflects the events handlers are given\n   750→\tif err := clientState.Replace(info.Objects, info.ResourceVersion); err != nil {\n   751→\t\treturn err\n   752→\t}\n   753→\t// Processing all deletions first matches behavior of RealFIFO#Replace\n   754→\tfor _, objToDelete := range deletions {\n   755→\t\thandler.OnDelete(objToDelete)\n   756→\t}\n   757→\t// Processing adds/updates in order observed by reconcileReplacement matches behavior of RealFIFO#Replace\n   758→\tfor _, r := range replacements {\n   759→\t\tif r.oldObj != nil {\n   760→\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(r.oldObj, r.newObj)\n   761→\t\t} else {\n   762→\t\t\thandler.OnAdd(r.newObj, isInInitialList)\n   763→\t\t}\n   764→\t}\n   765→\treturn nil\n   766→}\n   767→\n   768→// newInformer returns a controller for populating the store while also\n   769→// providing event notifications.\n   770→//\n   771→// Parameters\n   772→//   - clientState is the store you want to populate\n   773→//   - options contain the options to configure the controller\n   774→func newInformer(clientState Store, options InformerOptions, keyFunc KeyFunc) Controller {\n   775→\t// This will hold incoming changes. Note how we pass clientState in as a\n   776→\t// KeyLister, that way resync operations will result in the correct set\n   777→\t// of update/delete deltas.\n   778→\n   779→\tfifo := newQueueFIFO(clientState, options.Transform)\n   780→\n   781→\tcfg := &Config{\n   782→\t\tQueue:            fifo,\n   783→\t\tListerWatcher:    options.ListerWatcher,\n   784→\t\tObjectType:       options.ObjectType,\n   785→\t\tFullResyncPeriod: options.ResyncPeriod,\n   786→\t\tMinWatchTimeout:  options.MinWatchTimeout,\n   787→\n   788→\t\tProcess: func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) error {\n   789→\t\t\tif deltas, ok := obj.(Deltas); ok {\n   790→\t\t\t\treturn processDeltas(options.Handler, clientState, deltas, isInInitialList, keyFunc)\n   791→\t\t\t}\n   792→\t\t\treturn errors.New(\"object given as Process argument is not Deltas\")\n   793→\t\t},\n   794→\t\tProcessBatch: func(deltaList []Delta, isInInitialList bool) error {\n   795→\t\t\treturn processDeltasInBatch(options.Handler, clientState, deltaList, isInInitialList, keyFunc)\n   796→\t\t},\n   797→\t}\n   798→\treturn New(cfg)\n   799→}\n   800→\n   801→func newQueueFIFO(clientState Store, transform TransformFunc) Queue {\n   802→\tif clientgofeaturegate.FeatureGates().Enabled(clientgofeaturegate.InOrderInformers) {\n   803→\t\toptions := RealFIFOOptions{\n   804→\t\t\tKeyFunction: MetaNamespaceKeyFunc,\n   805→\t\t\tTransformer: transform,\n   806→\t\t}\n   807→\t\t// If atomic events are enabled, unset clientState in the case of atomic events as we cannot pass a\n   808→\t\t// store to an atomic fifo.\n   809→\t\tif clientgofeaturegate.FeatureGates().Enabled(clientgofeaturegate.AtomicFIFO) {\n   810→\t\t\toptions.AtomicEvents = true\n   811→\t\t} else {\n   812→\t\t\toptions.KnownObjects = clientState\n   813→\t\t}\n   814→\t\treturn NewRealFIFOWithOptions(options)\n   815→\t} else {\n   816→\t\treturn NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{\n   817→\t\t\tKnownObjects:          clientState,\n   818→\t\t\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced: true,\n   819→\t\t\tTransformer:           transform,\n   820→\t\t})\n   821→\t}\n   822→}\n   823→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Such informers, in turn, are key components\n// in the high level controllers that form the backbone of the\n// Kubernetes control plane.  Look at those for examples, or the\n// example in\n// https://github.com/kubernetes/client-go/tree/master/examples/workqueue\n// .\n\n// Config contains all the settings for one of these low-level controllers.\ntype Config struct {\n\t// The queue for your objects - has to be a DeltaFIFO due to\n\t// assumptions in the implementation. Your Process() function\n\t// should accept the output of this Queue's Pop() method.\n\tQueue\n\n\t// Something that can list and watch your objects.\n\tListerWatcher\n\n\t// Process can process a popped Deltas.\n\tProcess ProcessFunc\n\n\t// ProcessBatch can process a batch of popped Deltas, which should return `TransactionError` if not all items\n\t// in the batch were successfully processed.\n\t//\n\t// For batch processing to be used:\n\t// * ProcessBatch must be non-nil\n\t// * Queue must implement QueueWithBatch\n\t// * The client InOrderInformersBatchProcess feature gate must be enabled\n\t//\n\t// If any of those are false, Process is used and no batch processing is done.\n\tProcessBatch ProcessBatchFunc\n\n\t// ObjectType is an example object of the type this controller is\n\t// expected to handle.\n\tObjectType runtime.Object\n\n\t// ObjectDescription is the description to use when logging type-specific information about this controller.\n\tObjectDescription string\n\n\t// FullResyncPeriod is the period at which ShouldResync is considered.\n\tFullResyncPeriod time.Duration\n\n\t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\n\t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\n\t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\n\t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\n\tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\n\n\t// ShouldResync is periodically used by the reflector to determine\n\t// whether to Resync the Queue. If ShouldResync is `nil` or\n\t// returns true, it means the reflector should proceed with the\n\t// resync.\n\tShouldResync ShouldResyncFunc\n\n\t// Called whenever the ListAndWatch drops the connection with an error.\n\t//\n\t// Contextual logging: WatchErrorHandlerWithContext should be used instead of WatchErrorHandler in code which supports contextual logging.\n\tWatchErrorHandler WatchErrorHandler\n\n\t// Called whenever the ListAndWatch drops the connection with an error\n\t// and WatchErrorHandler is not set.\n\tWatchErrorHandlerWithContext WatchErrorHandlerWithContext\n\n\t// WatchListPageSize is the requested chunk size of initial and relist watch lists.\n\tWatchListPageSize int64\n}\n\n// ShouldResyncFunc is a type of function that indicates if a reflector should perform a\n// resync or not. It can be used by a shared informer to support multiple event handlers with custom\n// resync periods.\ntype ShouldResyncFunc func() bool\n\n// ProcessFunc processes a single object.\ntype ProcessFunc func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) error\n\n// ProcessBatchFunc processes multiple objects in batch.\n// The deltas must not contain multiple entries for the same object.\ntype ProcessBatchFunc func(deltas []Delta, isInInitialList bool) error\n\n// `*controller` implements Controller\ntype controller struct {\n\tconfig         Config\n\treflector      *Reflector\n\treflectorMutex sync.RWMutex\n\tclock          clock.Clock\n}\n\n// Controller is a low-level controller that is parameterized by a\n// Config and used in sharedIndexInformer.\ntype Controller interface {\n\t// RunWithContext does two things.  One is to construct and run a Reflector\n\t// to pump objects/notifications from the Config's ListerWatcher\n\t// to the Config's Queue and possibly invoke the occasional Resync\n\t// on that Queue.  The other is to repeatedly Pop from the Queue\n\t// and process with the Config's ProcessFunc.  Both of these\n\t// continue until the context is canceled.\n\t//\n\t// It's an error to call RunWithContext more than once.\n\t// RunWithContext blocks; call via go.\n\tRunWithContext(ctx context.Context)\n\n\t// Run does the same as RunWithContext with a stop channel instead of\n\t// a context.\n\t//\n\t// Contextual logging: RunWithcontext should be used instead of Run in code which supports contextual logging.\n\tRun(stopCh <-chan struct{})\n\n\t// HasSynced delegates to the Config's Queue\n\tHasSynced() bool\n\n\t// LastSyncResourceVersion delegates to the Reflector when there\n\t// is one, otherwise returns the empty string\n\tLastSyncResourceVersion() string\n}\n\n// New makes a new Controller from the given Config.\nfunc New(c *Config) Controller {\n\tctlr := &controller{\n\t\tconfig: *c,\n\t\tclock:  &clock.RealClock{},\n\t}\n\treturn ctlr\n}\n\n// Run implements [Controller.Run].\nfunc (c *controller) Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n\tc.RunWithContext(wait.ContextForChannel(stopCh))\n}\n\n// RunWithContext implements [Controller.RunWithContext].\nfunc (c *controller) RunWithContext(ctx context.Context) {\n\tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrashWithContext(ctx)\n\tgo func() {\n\t\t<-ctx.Done()\n\t\tc.config.Queue.Close()\n\t}()\n\tr := NewReflectorWithOptions(\n\t\tc.config.ListerWatcher,\n\t\tc.config.ObjectType,\n\t\tc.config.Queue,\n\t\tReflectorOptions{\n\t\t\tResyncPeriod:    c.config.FullResyncPeriod,\n\t\t\tMinWatchTimeout: c.config.MinWatchTimeout,\n\t\t\tTypeDescription: c.config.ObjectDescription,\n\t\t\tClock:           c.clock,\n\t\t},\n\t)\n\tr.ShouldResync = c.config.ShouldResync\n\tr.WatchListPageSize = c.config.WatchListPageSize\n\tif c.config.WatchErrorHandler != nil {\n\t\tr.watchErrorHandler = func(_ context.Context, r *Reflector, err error) {\n\t\t\tc.config.WatchErrorHandler(r, err)\n\t\t}\n\t} else if c.config.WatchErrorHandlerWithContext != nil {\n\t\tr.watchErrorHandler = c.config.WatchErrorHandlerWithContext\n\t}\n\n\tc.reflectorMutex.Lock()\n\tc.reflector = r\n\tc.reflectorMutex.Unlock()\n\n\tvar wg wait.Group\n\n\twg.StartWithContext(ctx, r.RunWithContext)\n\n\twait.UntilWithContext(ctx, c.processLoop, time.Second)\n\twg.Wait()\n}\n\n// Returns true once this controller has completed an initial resource listing\nfunc (c *controller) HasSynced() bool {\n\treturn c.config.Queue.HasSynced()\n}\n\nfunc (c *controller) LastSyncResourceVersion() string {\n\tc.reflectorMutex.RLock()\n\tdefer c.reflectorMutex.RUnlock()\n\tif c.reflector == nil {\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\treturn c.reflector.LastSyncResourceVersion()\n}\n\n// processLoop drains the work queue.\n// TODO: Consider doing the processing in parallel. This will require a little thought\n// to make sure that we don't end up processing the same object multiple times\n// concurrently.\nfunc (c *controller) processLoop(ctx context.Context) {\n\tuseBatchProcess := false\n\tbatchQueue, ok := c.config.Queue.(QueueWithBatch)\n\tif ok && c.config.ProcessBatch != nil && clientgofeaturegate.FeatureGates().Enabled(clientgofeaturegate.InOrderInformersBatchProcess) {\n\t\tuseBatchProcess = true\n\t}\n\tfor {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tvar err error\n\t\t\tif useBatchProcess {\n\t\t\t\terr = batchQueue.PopBatch(c.config.ProcessBatch, PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// otherwise fallback to non-batch process behavior\n\t\t\t\t_, err = c.config.Pop(PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tif errors.Is(err, ErrFIFOClosed) {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// ResourceEventHandler can handle notifications for events that\n// happen to a resource. The events are informational only, so you\n// can't return an error.  The handlers MUST NOT modify the objects\n// received; this concerns not only the top level of structure but all\n// the data structures reachable from it.\n//   - OnAdd is called when an object is added.\n//   - OnUpdate is called when an object is modified. Note that oldObj is the\n//     last known state of the object-- it is possible that several changes\n//     were combined together, so you can't use this to see every single\n//     change. OnUpdate is also called when a re-list happens, and it will\n//     get called even if nothing changed. This is useful for periodically\n//     evaluating or syncing something.\n//   - OnDelete will get the final state of the item if it is known, otherwise\n//     it will get an object of type DeletedFinalStateUnknown. This can\n//     happen if the watch is closed and misses the delete event and we don't\n//     notice the deletion until the subsequent re-list.\ntype ResourceEventHandler interface {\n\tOnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\n\tOnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n\tOnDelete(obj interface{})\n}\n\n// ResourceEventHandlerFuncs is an adaptor to let you easily specify as many or\n// as few of the notification functions as you want while still implementing\n// ResourceEventHandler.  This adapter does not remove the prohibition against\n// modifying the objects.\n//\n// See ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs if your use needs to propagate\n// HasSynced.\ntype ResourceEventHandlerFuncs struct {\n\tAddFunc    func(obj interface{})\n\tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n\tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\n}\n\n// OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n\tif r.AddFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.AddFunc(obj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs is exactly like ResourceEventHandlerFuncs\n// except its AddFunc accepts the isInInitialList parameter, for propagating\n// HasSynced.\ntype ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs struct {\n\tAddFunc    func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\n\tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n\tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\n}\n\n// OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n\tif r.AddFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.AddFunc(obj, isInInitialList)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// FilteringResourceEventHandler applies the provided filter to all events coming\n// in, ensuring the appropriate nested handler method is invoked. An object\n// that starts passing the filter after an update is considered an add, and an\n// object that stops passing the filter after an update is considered a delete.\n// Like the handlers, the filter MUST NOT modify the objects it is given.\ntype FilteringResourceEventHandler struct {\n\tFilterFunc func(obj interface{}) bool\n\tHandler    ResourceEventHandler\n}\n\n// OnAdd calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\nfunc (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tr.Handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n}\n\n// OnUpdate ensures the proper handler is called depending on whether the filter matches\nfunc (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n\tnewer := r.FilterFunc(newObj)\n\tolder := r.FilterFunc(oldObj)\n\tswitch {\n\tcase newer && older:\n\t\tr.Handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\n\tcase newer && !older:\n\t\tr.Handler.OnAdd(newObj, false)\n\tcase !newer && older:\n\t\tr.Handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\n\tdefault:\n\t\t// do nothing\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnDelete calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\nfunc (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tr.Handler.OnDelete(obj)\n}\n\n// DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc checks for\n// DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n// MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\nfunc DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj interface{}) (string, error) {\n\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n\t\treturn d.Key, nil\n\t}\n\treturn MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n}\n\n// DeletionHandlingObjectToName checks for\n// DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n// ObjectToName.\nfunc DeletionHandlingObjectToName(obj interface{}) (ObjectName, error) {\n\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n\t\treturn ParseObjectName(d.Key)\n\t}\n\treturn ObjectToName(obj)\n}\n\n// InformerOptions configure a Reflector.\ntype InformerOptions struct {\n\t// ListerWatcher implements List and Watch functions for the source of the resource\n\t// the informer will be informing about.\n\tListerWatcher ListerWatcher\n\n\t// ObjectType is an object of the type that informer is expected to receive.\n\tObjectType runtime.Object\n\n\t// Handler defines functions that should called on object mutations.\n\tHandler ResourceEventHandler\n\n\t// ResyncPeriod is the underlying Reflector's resync period. If non-zero, the store\n\t// is re-synced with that frequency - Modify events are delivered even if objects\n\t// didn't change.\n\t// This is useful for synchronizing objects that configure external resources\n\t// (e.g. configure cloud provider functionalities).\n\t// Optional - if unset, store resyncing is not happening periodically.\n\tResyncPeriod time.Duration\n\n\t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\n\t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\n\t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\n\t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\n\tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\n\n\t// Indexers, if set, are the indexers for the received objects to optimize\n\t// certain queries.\n\t// Optional - if unset no indexes are maintained.\n\tIndexers Indexers\n\n\t// Transform function, if set, will be called on all objects before they will be\n\t// put into the Store and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will be invoked\n\t// for them.\n\t// Optional - if unset no additional transforming is happening.\n\tTransform TransformFunc\n}\n\n// NewInformerWithOptions returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\n// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n// Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n// notifications to be faulty.\nfunc NewInformerWithOptions(options InformerOptions) (Store, Controller) {\n\tvar clientState Store\n\tif options.Indexers == nil {\n\t\tclientState = NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n\t} else {\n\t\tclientState = NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, options.Indexers)\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n}\n\n// NewInformer returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\n// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n// Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n// notifications to be faulty.\n//\n// Parameters:\n//   - lw is list and watch functions for the source of the resource you want to\n//     be informed of.\n//   - objType is an object of the type that you expect to receive.\n//   - resyncPeriod: if non-zero, will re-list this often (you will get OnUpdate\n//     calls, even if nothing changed). Otherwise, re-list will be delayed as\n//     long as possible (until the upstream source closes the watch or times out,\n//     or you stop the controller).\n//   - h is the object you want notifications sent to.\n//\n// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\nfunc NewInformer(\n\tlw ListerWatcher,\n\tobjType runtime.Object,\n\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n\th ResourceEventHandler,\n) (Store, Controller) {\n\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n\tclientState := NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n\n\toptions := InformerOptions{\n\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n\t\tHandler:       h,\n\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n}\n\n// NewIndexerInformer returns an Indexer and a Controller for populating the index\n// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n// Index for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n// notifications to be faulty.\n//\n// Parameters:\n//   - lw is list and watch functions for the source of the resource you want to\n//     be informed of.\n//   - objType is an object of the type that you expect to receive.\n//   - resyncPeriod: if non-zero, will re-list this often (you will get OnUpdate\n//     calls, even if nothing changed). Otherwise, re-list will be delayed as\n//     long as possible (until the upstream source closes the watch or times out,\n//     or you stop the controller).\n//   - h is the object you want notifications sent to.\n//   - indexers is the indexer for the received object type.\n//\n// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\nfunc NewIndexerInformer(\n\tlw ListerWatcher,\n\tobjType runtime.Object,\n\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n\th ResourceEventHandler,\n\tindexers Indexers,\n) (Indexer, Controller) {\n\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n\tclientState := NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, indexers)\n\n\toptions := InformerOptions{\n\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n\t\tHandler:       h,\n\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n\t\tIndexers:      indexers,\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n}\n\n// NewTransformingInformer returns a Store and a controller for populating\n// the store while also providing event notifications. You should only used\n// the returned Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause\n// the event notifications to be faulty.\n// The given transform function will be called on all objects before they will\n// put into the Store and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will\n// be invoked for them.\n//\n// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\nfunc NewTransformingInformer(\n\tlw ListerWatcher,\n\tobjType runtime.Object,\n\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n\th ResourceEventHandler,\n\ttransformer TransformFunc,\n) (Store, Controller) {\n\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n\tclientState := NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n\n\toptions := InformerOptions{\n\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n\t\tHandler:       h,\n\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n\t\tTransform:     transformer,\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n}\n\n// NewTransformingIndexerInformer returns an Indexer and a controller for\n// populating the index while also providing event notifications. You should\n// only used the returned Index for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes\n// will cause the event notifications to be faulty.\n// The given transform function will be called on all objects before they will\n// be put into the Index and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will\n// be invoked for them.\n//\n// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\nfunc NewTransformingIndexerInformer(\n\tlw ListerWatcher,\n\tobjType runtime.Object,\n\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n\th ResourceEventHandler,\n\tindexers Indexers,\n\ttransformer TransformFunc,\n) (Indexer, Controller) {\n\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n\tclientState := NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, indexers)\n\n\toptions := InformerOptions{\n\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n\t\tHandler:       h,\n\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n\t\tIndexers:      indexers,\n\t\tTransform:     transformer,\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n}\n\n// Multiplexes updates in the form of a list of Deltas into a Store, and informs\n// a given handler of events OnUpdate, OnAdd, OnDelete\nfunc processDeltas(\n\t// Object which receives event notifications from the given deltas\n\thandler ResourceEventHandler,\n\tclientState Store,\n\tdeltas Deltas,\n\tisInInitialList bool,\n\tkeyFunc KeyFunc,\n) error {\n\t// from oldest to newest\n\tfor _, d := range deltas {\n\t\tobj := d.Object\n\n\t\tswitch d.Type {\n\t\tcase ReplacedAll:\n\t\t\tinfo, ok := obj.(ReplacedAllInfo)\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"ReplacedAll did not contain ReplacedAllInfo: %T\", obj)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif err := processReplacedAllInfo(handler, info, clientState, isInInitialList, keyFunc); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase SyncAll:\n\t\t\t_, ok := obj.(SyncAllInfo)\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"SyncAll did not contain SyncAllInfo: %T\", obj)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tobjs := clientState.List()\n\t\t\tfor _, obj := range objs {\n\t\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(obj, obj)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\tcase Sync, Replaced, Added, Updated:\n\t\t\tif old, exists, err := clientState.Get(obj); err == nil && exists {\n\t\t\t\tif err := clientState.Update(obj); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(old, obj)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tif err := clientState.Add(obj); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\thandler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase Deleted:\n\t\t\tif err := clientState.Delete(obj); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\thandler.OnDelete(obj)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// processDeltasInBatch applies a batch of Delta objects to the given Store and\n// notifies the ResourceEventHandler of add, update, or delete events.\n//\n// If the Store supports transactions (TransactionStore), all Deltas are applied\n// atomically in a single transaction and corresponding handler callbacks are\n// executed afterward. Otherwise, each Delta is processed individually.\n//\n// Returns an error if any Delta or transaction fails. For TransactionError,\n// only successful operations trigger callbacks.\nfunc processDeltasInBatch(\n\thandler ResourceEventHandler,\n\tclientState Store,\n\tdeltas []Delta,\n\tisInInitialList bool,\n\tkeyFunc KeyFunc,\n) error {\n\t// from oldest to newest\n\ttxns := make([]Transaction, 0)\n\tcallbacks := make([]func(), 0)\n\ttxnStore, txnSupported := clientState.(TransactionStore)\n\tif !txnSupported {\n\t\tvar errs []error\n\t\tfor _, delta := range deltas {\n\t\t\tif err := processDeltas(handler, clientState, Deltas{delta}, isInInitialList, keyFunc); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\terrs = append(errs, err)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tif len(errs) > 0 {\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected error when handling deltas: %v\", errs)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\t// deltasList is a list of unique objects\n\tfor _, d := range deltas {\n\t\tobj := d.Object\n\t\tswitch d.Type {\n\t\tcase Sync, Replaced, Added, Updated:\n\t\t\t// it will only return one old object for each because items are unique\n\t\t\tif old, exists, err := clientState.Get(obj); err == nil && exists {\n\t\t\t\ttxn := Transaction{\n\t\t\t\t\tType:   TransactionTypeUpdate,\n\t\t\t\t\tObject: obj,\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\ttxns = append(txns, txn)\n\t\t\t\tcallbacks = append(callbacks, func() {\n\t\t\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(old, obj)\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\ttxn := Transaction{\n\t\t\t\t\tType:   TransactionTypeAdd,\n\t\t\t\t\tObject: obj,\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\ttxns = append(txns, txn)\n\t\t\t\tcallbacks = append(callbacks, func() {\n\t\t\t\t\thandler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase Deleted:\n\t\t\ttxn := Transaction{\n\t\t\t\tType:   TransactionTypeDelete,\n\t\t\t\tObject: obj,\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\ttxns = append(txns, The resync operation\n   154→\t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\n   155→\t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\n   156→\t// any interactions with the authoritative storage.  Some\n   157→\t// informers do no resyncs at all, not even for handlers added\n   158→\t// with a non-zero resyncPeriod.  For an informer that does\n   159→\t// resyncs, and for each handler that requests resyncs, that\n   160→\t// informer develops a nominal resync period that is no shorter\n   161→\t// than the requested period but may be longer.  The actual time\n   162→\t// between any two resyncs may be longer than the nominal period\n   163→\t// because the implementation takes time to do work and there may\n   164→\t// be competing load and scheduling noise.\n   165→\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to remove\n   166→\t// the handler again and an error if the handler cannot be added.\n   167→\t//\n   168→\t// Contextual logging: AddEventHandlerWithOptions together with a logger in the options should be used instead of AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod in code which supports contextual logging.\n   169→\tAddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod(handler ResourceEventHandler, resyncPeriod time.Duration) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n   170→\t// AddEventHandlerWithOptions is a All are\n    32→// optional.\n    33→type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\n    34→\n    35→\t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\n    36→\t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\n    37→\t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\n    38→\t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\n    39→\tKeyFunction KeyFunc\n    40→\n    41→\t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\n    42→\t// this queue \"knows about\". It is used to decide which items are missing\n    43→\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\n    44→\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\n    45→\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\n    46→\n    47→\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\n    48→\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\n    49→\t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\n    50→\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\n    51→\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\n    52→\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\n    53→\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n    54→\n    55→\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\n    56→\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\n    57→\tTransformer TransformFunc\n    58→\n    59→\t// If set, log output will go to this logger instead of klog.Background().\n    60→\tLogger *klog.Logger\n    61→}\n    62→\n    63→// DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\n    64→// accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\n    65→// but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\n    66→// object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n    67→// except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n    68→// Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n    69→// not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n    70→// Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n    71→// DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n    72→//\n    73→// The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n    74→// an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n    75→// If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n    76→// replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\n    77→// resync events.\n    78→//\n    79→// DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n    80→// intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n    81→// the Pop() method.\n    82→//\n    83→// DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n    84→//   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n    85→//   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n    86→//     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n    87→//   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n    88→//   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n    89→//\n    90→// DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n    91→// interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n    92→// will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\n    93→// the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\n    94→//\n    95→// A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\n    96→// to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\n    97→// question are called \"known objects\" and this set of objects\n    98→// modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\n    99→// (each in a different way).\n   100→//\n   101→// A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\n   102→// threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\n   103→// different versions of the same object.\n   104→type DeltaFIFO struct {\n   105→\t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\n   106→\tlock sync.RWMutex\n   107→\tcond sync.Cond\n   108→\n   109→\t// `items` maps a key to a Deltas.\n   110→\t// Each such Deltas has at least one Delta.\n   111→\titems map[string]Deltas\n   112→\n   113→\t// `queue` maintains FIFO order of keys for consumption in Pop().\n   114→\t// There are no duplicates in `queue`.\n   115→\t// A key is in `queue` if and only if it is in `items`.\n   116→\tqueue []string\n   117→\n   118→\t// populated is true if the first All are\n// optional.\ntype DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\n\n\t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\n\t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\n\t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\n\t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\n\tKeyFunction KeyFunc\n\n\t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\n\t// this queue \"knows about\". It is used to decide which items are missing\n\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\n\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\n\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\n\n\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\n\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\n\t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\n\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\n\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\n\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\n\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n\n\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\n\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\n\tTransformer TransformFunc\n\n\t// If set, log output will go to this logger instead of klog.Background().\n\tLogger *klog.Logger\n}\n\n// DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\n// accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\n// but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\n// object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n// except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n// Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n// not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n// Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n// DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n//\n// The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n// an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n// If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n// replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\n// resync events.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n// intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n// the Pop() method.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n//   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n//   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n//     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n//   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n//   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n// interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n// will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\n// the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\n//\n// A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\n// to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\n// question are called \"known objects\" and this set of objects\n// modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\n// (each in a different way).\n//\n// A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\n// threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\n// different versions of the same object.\ntype DeltaFIFO struct {\n\t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\n\tlock sync.RWMutex\n\tcond sync.Cond\n\n\t// `items` maps a key to a Deltas.\n\t// Each such Deltas has at least one Delta.\n\titems map[string]Deltas\n\n\t// `queue` maintains FIFO order of keys for consumption in Pop().\n\t// There are no duplicates in `queue`.\n\t// A key is in `queue` if and only if it is in `items`.\n\tqueue []string\n\n\t// populated is true if the first batch of items inserted by Replace() has been populated\n\t// or Delete/Add/Update/AddIfNotPresent was called first.\n\tpopulated bool\n\t// initialPopulationCount is the number of items inserted by the first call of Replace()\n\tinitialPopulationCount int\n\n\t// keyFunc is used to make the key used for queued item\n\t// insertion and retrieval, and should be deterministic.\n\tkeyFunc KeyFunc\n\n\t// knownObjects list keys that are \"known\" --- affecting Delete(),\n\t// Replace(), and Resync()\n\tknownObjects KeyListerGetter\n\n\t// Used to indicate a queue is closed so a control loop can exit when a queue is empty.\n\t// Currently, not used to gate any of CRUD operations.\n\tclosed bool\n\n\t// emitDeltaTypeReplaced is whether to emit the Replaced or Sync\n\t// DeltaType when Replace() is called (to preserve backwards compat).\n\temitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n\n\t// Called with every object if non-nil.\n\ttransformer TransformFunc\n\n\t// logger is a per-instance logger. This gets chosen when constructing\n\t// the instance, with klog.Background() as default.\n\tlogger klog.Logger\n}\n\n// TransformFunc allows for transforming an object before it will be processed.\n//\n// The most common usage pattern is to clean-up some parts of the object to","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":746}}}

Every\n\t// element of queue should be in the dirty set and not in the\n\t// processing set.\n\tqueue Queue[t]\n\n\t// dirty defines all of the items that need to be processed.\n\tdirty sets.Set[t]\n\n\t// Things that are currently being processed are in the processing set.\n\t// These things may be simultaneously in the dirty set. When we finish\n\t// processing something and remove it from this set, we'll check if\n\t// it's in the dirty set, and if so, add it to the queue.\n\tprocessing sets.Set[t]\n\n\tcond *sync.Cond\n\n\tshuttingDown bool\n\tdrain        bool\n\n\tmetrics queueMetrics[t]\n\n\tunfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod time.Duration\n\tclock                      clock.WithTicker\n\n\t// wg manages goroutines started by the queue to allow graceful shutdown\n\t// ShutDown() will wait for goroutines to exit before returning.\n\twg sync.WaitGroup\n\n\tstopCh chan struct{}\n\t// stopOnce guarantees we only signal shutdown a single time\n\tstopOnce sync.Once\n}\n\n// Add marks item as needing processing. When the queue is shutdown new\n// items will silently be ignored and not queued or marked as dirty for\n// reprocessing.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Add(item T) {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\tif q.shuttingDown {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tif q.dirty.Has(item) {\n\t\t// the same item is added again before it is processed, call the Touch\n\t\t// function if the queue cares about it (for e.g, reset its priority)\n\t\tif !q.processing.Has(item) {\n\t\t\tq.queue.Touch(item)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tq.metrics.add(item)\n\n\tq.dirty.Insert(item)\n\tif q.processing.Has(item) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tq.queue.Push(item)\n\tq.cond.Signal()\n}\n\n// Len returns the current queue length, for informational purposes only. You\n// shouldn't e.g. gate a call to Add() or Get() on Len() being a particular\n// value, that can't be synchronized properly.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Len() int {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\treturn q.queue.Len()\n}\n\n// Get blocks until it can return an item to be processed. If shutdown = true,\n// the caller should end their goroutine. You must call Done with item when you\n// have finished processing it.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Get() (item T, shutdown bool) {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\tfor q.queue.Len() == 0 && !q.shuttingDown {\n\t\tq.cond.Wait()\n\t}\n\tif q.queue.Len() == 0 {\n\t\t// We must be shutting down.\n\t\treturn *new(T), true\n\t}\n\n\titem = q.queue.Pop()\n\n\tq.metrics.get(item)\n\n\tq.processing.Insert(item)\n\tq.dirty.Delete(item)\n\n\treturn item, false\n}\n\n// Done marks item as done processing, and if it has been marked as dirty again\n// while it was being processed, it will be re-added to the queue for\n// re-processing.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Done(item T) {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\tq.metrics.done(item)\n\n\tq.processing.Delete(item)\n\tif q.dirty.Has(item) {\n\t\tq.queue.Push(item)\n\t\tq.cond.Signal()\n\t} else if q.processing.Len() == 0 {\n\t\tq.cond.Signal()\n\t}\n}\n\n// ShutDown will cause q to ignore all new items added to it. Worker\n// goroutines will continue processing items in the queue until it is\n// empty and then receive the shutdown signal.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) ShutDown() {\n\tdefer q.wg.Wait()\n\tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\n\t\tdefer close(q.stopCh)\n\t})\n\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\tq.drain = false\n\tq.shuttingDown = true\n\tq.cond.Broadcast()\n}\n\n// ShutDownWithDrain is equivalent to ShutDown but waits until all items\n// in the queue have been processed.\n// ShutDown can be called after ShutDownWithDrain to force\n// ShutDownWithDrain to stop waiting.\n// Workers must call Done on an item after processing it, otherwise\n// ShutDownWithDrain will block indefinitely.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) ShutDownWithDrain() {\n\tdefer q.wg.Wait()\n\tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\n\t\tdefer close(q.stopCh)\n\t})\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\tq.drain = true\n\tq.shuttingDown = true\n\tq.cond.Broadcast()\n\n\tfor q.processing.Len() != 0 && q.drain {\n\t\tq.cond.Wait()\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) ShuttingDown() bool {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\treturn q.shuttingDown\n}\n\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) updateUnfinishedWork() {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\tif !q.shuttingDown {\n\t\tq.metrics.updateUnfinishedWork()\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) updateUnfinishedWorkLoop() {\n\tt := q.clock.NewTicker(q.unfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod)\n\tdefer t.Stop()\n\tfor {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase <-t.C():\n\t\t\tq.updateUnfinishedWork()\n\t\tcase <-q.stopCh:\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n","numLines":371,"startLine":1,"totalLines":371}}}

true\n\t\t\tlistener.determineNextResync(now)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn resyncNeeded\n}\n\nfunc (p *sharedProcessor) resyncCheckPeriodChanged(logger klog.Logger, resyncCheckPeriod time.Duration)
