{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01BzGDSLeo3jnXUwafbg7z5q","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_019skFaL92iKEi8pR56PWYja","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# client-go: An Advanced Systems Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n`client-go` is the official Go client library for the Kubernetes API. It sits at the intersection of every controller, operator, and internal control-plane component in the Kubernetes ecosystem. Its role is to:\n\n- Provide authenticated, rate-limited, retry-capable HTTP access to the kube-apiserver's REST API.\n- Abstract the list/watch protocol into an eventually-consistent local cache (the *informer* machinery).\n- Expose a work-queue primitive that decouples event receipt from reconciliation, enabling a well-known controller pattern.\n- Offer ancillary facilities: leader election, port forwarding, remote command execution, and structured metrics.\n\n**Upstream dependencies.** `client-go` depends on `k8s.io/apimachinery` for API object types, serializers, and the watch event protocol, and on `k8s.io/api` for the concrete Kubernetes object types. It imports `k8s.io/utils` for clock abstraction (test seam), exponential backoff, and buffer utilities.\n\n**Downstream consumers.** Every Kubernetes built-in controller (scheduler, node-controller, endpoint-slice controller, etc.) uses `client-go`. Third-party operators and `controller-runtime`-based projects sit on top of the same informer/work-queue contract. The API server itself uses `client-go` for its own internal clients when it acts as a consumer (e.g. admission webhooks with client access).\n\n**Staging location.** The authoritative source lives under `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/` in the main Kubernetes repository and is published as a standalone module. All references in this document use the staging path.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Boundaries\n\nThe library divides cleanly into four layers:\n\n### 2.1 REST Layer (`rest/`)\n\nThe REST layer is the raw transport. Key files:\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `rest/config.go` | `Config` struct – holds credentials, QPS, burst, TLS, `WrapTransport` |\n| `rest/client.go` | `RESTClient` – root URL, rate limiter, content negotiation, `http.Client` |\n| `rest/request.go` | `Request` – fluent builder for a single HTTP call |\n| `rest/with_retry.go` | `WithRetry` interface – per-request retry policy |\n\n`RESTClient` (`rest/client.go:86`) holds an `http.Client`, a root URL, and a `flowcontrol.RateLimiter`. It provides verb-oriented factory methods (`Get()`, `Post()`, `Verb(v)`) that return a `*Request`. The `Request` object accumulates the resource path, query parameters, body, and headers, then executes the call via `Do(ctx)` or opens a watch stream via `Watch(ctx)`.\n\n`rest/config.go` exposes `DefaultQPS = 5.0` and `DefaultBurst = 10` as the built-in rate-limit knobs. QPS / Burst together feed a token-bucket rate limiter whose delay is logged when it exceeds `longThrottleLatency = 50ms` (`rest/request.go:57–61`).\n\n`rest/with_retry.go` defines `WithRetry`, which governs whether a failed request is retried. The default implementation backs off on 429 and 5xx responses and rewinds the request body before retrying.\n\n### 2.2 Informer Machinery (`tools/cache/`)\n\nThis is the heart of the controller pattern. It comprises five cooperating types:\n\n#### Reflector (`tools/cache/reflector.go`)\n\nThe `Reflector` owns the connection to the API server for a single resource type. It is instantiated with a `ListerWatcher` and a target `ReflectorStore`, and runs a continuous `ListAndWatchWithContext` loop (`reflector.go:408`):\n\n1. On startup (or after a watch failure), it issues a **List** call (paginated via `tools/pager`) to populate the store with an initial snapshot, recording the resulting `ResourceVersion`.\n2. If the `WatchListClient` feature gate is enabled (beta as of v1.35, `features/known_features.go:89`), it can instead open a streaming **WatchList** request that returns items as a watch stream, avoiding the full list-then-watch round trip.\n3. It then opens a `Watch` call from that `ResourceVersion`, consuming `watch.Event` objects and routing them to the store via `store.Add`, `store.Update`, `store.Delete`, or `store.Replace`.\n4. On watch termination it calls `watchErrorHandler` and restarts via an exponential back-off manager seeded at 800 ms, capped at 30 s (`reflector.go:282`).\n5. Concurrently, `startResync` fires the store's `Resync()` at the configured period, triggering re-delivery of Sync deltas for all known objects.\n\nThe watch timeout is randomized in `[minWatchTimeout, 2*minWatchTimeout]` (default 5–10 min) to spread load across many watchers (`reflector.go:526–536`). Bookmarks (`AllowWatchBookmarks: true`) are always requested to advance `lastSyncResourceVersion` without requiring a full re-list.\n\n#### DeltaFIFO / RealFIFO (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`, `tools/cache/the_real_fifo.go`)\n\nThe `DeltaFIFO` is the staging queue between the Reflector (producer) and the controller's `processLoop` (consumer). Its defining characteristic is that it accumulates **change history** (Deltas) keyed by object identity, not just the latest state.\n\nA Delta has a type (`Added`, `Updated`, `Deleted`, `Replaced`, `Sync`) and an object. When the same object key is enqueued multiple times before the consumer pops it, the accumulator grows:\n\n```\nkey \"default/pod-a\" → [Delta{Sync, pod-a-v1}, Delta{Updated, pod-a-v2}]\n```\n\n`Pop()` dequeues an entire `Deltas` slice under lock and calls the `ProcessFunc` while still holding it. This design means the controller sees every intermediate state, never skips a change, and can detect the difference between a net-new object and an update.\n\nWhen the `InOrderInformers` feature gate is enabled (beta, on by default since v1.33 – `known_features.go:66`), the queue is a `RealFIFO` instead of `DeltaFIFO`. `RealFIFO` delivers events in strict arrival order and, when `UnlockWhileProcessingFIFO` is also enabled, releases the queue lock during `ProcessFunc` execution to allow concurrent producers to continue adding events.\n\nThe `KnownObjects` reference back to the downstream `Store` is critical: during a `Replace()` call (initial list or re-list), `DeltaFIFO` computes the symmetric difference between the listed keys and `KnownObjects.ListKeys()` to synthesize `Deleted` deltas for any objects that have vanished.\n\n#### Store / Indexer (`tools/cache/store.go`, `tools/cache/index.go`, `tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`)\n\nThe `Store` interface (`store.go:41`) is a keyed map of live objects with `Add`, `Update`, `Delete`, `List`, `Get`, `GetByKey`, `Replace`, and `Resync` methods. The concrete implementation is `cache` (lowercase, unexported), which wraps a `ThreadSafeStore`.\n\n`ThreadSafeStore` (`thread_safe_store.go:43`) couples a `sync.RWMutex`-protected object map with a `storeIndex` – the secondary index structure. An `Indexer` (`index.go:35`) extends `Store` with `Index`, `ByIndex`, `IndexKeys`, and `ListIndexFuncValues`. Callers register `IndexFunc` functions (returning a slice of string keys) under named indexes; the `NamespaceIndex` / `MetaNamespaceIndexFunc` pair is the canonical example, mapping objects to their namespace.\n\nLookups like `informer.GetIndexer().ByIndex(\"namespace\", \"kube-system\")` are O(1) set lookups, not linear scans – the store maintains an inverted index (map[indexedValue]set[storageKey]).\n\n#### sharedIndexInformer (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`)\n\n`sharedIndexInformer` (`shared_informer.go:420`) is the user-facing type. It owns three sub-components:\n\n1. **`indexer Indexer`** – the live object cache, described above.\n2. **`controller Controller`** – a low-level controller (`tools/cache/controller.go:114`) that runs the Reflector and the processLoop.\n3. **`processor *sharedProcessor`** – fan-out relay to N registered event handlers.\n\nThe controller's `ProcessFunc` is `sharedIndexInformer.HandleDeltas`, which (under a `blockDeltas` mutex) applies each delta to `indexer` then notifies the `sharedProcessor`. The mutex prevents a race between late-joining handlers (which replay the existing cache) and live delta processing.\n\n`sharedProcessor` (`shared_informer.go:803`) holds a map of `*processorListener` values. Each listener has two goroutines: `pop` drains a channel and transfers notifications to a ring-buffer (`k8s.io/utils/buffer`), and `run` drains the buffer and calls the user's `ResourceEventHandler`. This two-goroutine design decouples a slow handler from stalling the distribution path. Resync-only notifications are filtered per-listener based on each listener's `resyncPeriod`, allowing different handlers to request different resync cadences from the same underlying informer connection.\n\n#### SharedInformerFactory (`informers/factory.go`)\n\n`sharedInformerFactory` (`factory.go:57`) is a registry of one `SharedIndexInformer` per `reflect.Type`. When code calls `factory.Core().V1().Pods().Informer()`, the factory lazily constructs the informer (if absent), stores it keyed by `reflect.TypeOf(&v1.Pod{})`, and returns the shared instance. All callers that request the same type share a single Reflector and a single store, so one watch connection services all controllers interested in Pods.\n\n`factory.Start(stopCh)` (`factory.go:144`) iterates the map and starts each not-yet-started informer in its own goroutine. `WaitForCacheSync` polls `informer.HasSynced()` at 100 ms intervals until all informers report that the initial list has been processed.\n\n### 2.3 Work Queue (`util/workqueue/`)\n\nThe work queue decouples informer event delivery from the reconciliation loop. Key files:\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `util/workqueue/queue.go` | Base `Typed[T]` queue with deduplication |\n| `util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go` | Adds `AddAfter(item, delay)` |\n| `util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go` | Adds `AddRateLimited`, `Forget`, `NumRequeues` |\n| `util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go` | Built-in rate limiter implementations |\n\n`Typed[T]` (`queue.go:190`) maintains three data structures under a single mutex:\n\n- **`queue Queue[T]`** – ordered FIFO of items to be processed (no duplicates at any moment).\n- **`dirty sets.Set[T]`** – the union of queued and currently-processing items that are pending.\n- **`processing sets.Set[T]`** – items currently held by a `Get()` caller.\n\n`Add(item)` inserts into `dirty`. If the item is already in `processing`, it does not enqueue it again – instead the item remains in `dirty` and is re-enqueued when `Done(item)` is called. This guarantees that if an object changes while it is being reconciled, reconciliation runs again, but never more than once per pending change.\n\n`TypedRateLimitingInterface` (`rate_limiting_queue.go:27`) wraps a `TypedDelayingInterface` (which uses a min-heap for delayed delivery) and delegates rate decisions to a `TypedRateLimiter`. The **default rate limiter** (`default_rate_limiters.go:50`) composites two limiters via `MaxOfRateLimiter`:\n\n- `ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter`: per-item back-off starting at 5 ms, doubling on each failure, capped at 1000 s.\n- `BucketRateLimiter`: token-bucket at 10 QPS / burst 100, global across all items.\n\nThe composite means an item that fails repeatedly backs off exponentially (protecting the API server from hammering), while the global bucket prevents a large burst of distinct keys from flooding it.\n\n### 2.4 Ancillary Tools\n\n- **`tools/leaderelection/`** – distributed leader election using Kubernetes `Lease`, `ConfigMap`, or `Endpoints` objects as a lock. Tolerant of arbitrary clock skew; tunable via `LeaseDuration`, `RenewDeadline`, and `RetryPeriod` (`leaderelection.go:76–101`). Provides `OnStartedLeading`, `OnStoppedLeading`, and `OnNewLeader` callbacks.\n- **`tools/clientcmd/`** – kubeconfig parsing, merging, and REST config construction from KUBECONFIG files or in-cluster service account tokens.\n- **`transport/`** – TLS configuration, exec-based credential plugins, and `WrapperFunc` chain for pluggable authentication middleware.\n- **`util/flowcontrol/`** – token-bucket `RateLimiter` used directly by `RESTClient`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\nThis section traces the full path from a Kubernetes object change to a controller reconciling it.\n\n### 3.1 Phase 1: Startup\n\n```\ncontroller binary\n  └── NewSharedInformerFactory(client, resyncPeriod)   [informers/factory.go:112]\n       └── factory.Core().V1().Pods().Informer()\n            └── factory.InformerFor(&v1.Pod{}, newPodInformer)  [factory.go:200]\n                 └── NewSharedIndexInformerWithOptions(lw, &v1.Pod{}, opts) [shared_informer.go:303]\n                      └── sharedIndexInformer{\n                            indexer:    NewIndexer(MetaNamespaceKeyFunc, opts.Indexers),\n                            processor:  &sharedProcessor{},\n                            listerWatcher: lw,\n                          }\n```\n\nThe factory's `InformerFor` is idempotent – calling it twice with the same type returns the same instance.\n\n### 3.2 Phase 2: Running\n\n`factory.Start(stopCh)` spawns one goroutine per informer type: `go informer.Run(stopCh)`.\n\nInside `sharedIndexInformer.RunWithContext` (`shared_informer.go:537`):\n\n1. A `DeltaFIFO` (or `RealFIFO` if `InOrderInformers` is enabled) is created with `s.indexer` as `KnownObjects`.\n2. A `Config` is built connecting the FIFO to `HandleDeltas` as the `ProcessFunc`.\n3. A `controller` is created and run: it spawns a `Reflector.RunWithContext` goroutine and then enters `processLoop`.\n4. The `sharedProcessor.run` goroutine starts all listener goroutine pairs.\n\n### 3.3 Phase 3: Initial List\n\n`Reflector.ListAndWatchWithContext` (`reflector.go:408`) calls `r.list(ctx)`, which:\n\n1. Issues a paginated LIST (via `tools/pager`) at `ResourceVersion=\"\"` (consistent read from etcd).\n2. Calls `r.store.Replace(items, resourceVersion)` on the DeltaFIFO.\n3. `DeltaFIFO.Replace` computes deletion deltas for objects in `KnownObjects` not in the list, then enqueues `Replaced` deltas for all listed objects.\n\n`processLoop` pops each `Deltas` slice and calls `HandleDeltas`, which in turn calls `processDeltas` (`controller.go:581`). For each delta of type `Replaced`/`Added`:\n\n- If the object exists in `indexer`: call `indexer.Update(obj)` then `handler.OnUpdate(old, obj)`.\n- Otherwise: call `indexer.Add(obj)` then `handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList=true)`.\n\n`sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd` calls `processor.distribute(addNotification{...}, false)`, which fans out to every `processorListener.add(...)`. Each listener's `pop` goroutine buffers the notification; `run` drains the buffer and calls the user's `ResourceEventHandler.OnAdd`.\n\nAfter all `Replace` deltas are processed, `controller.HasSynced()` returns `true`, unblocking any `WaitForCacheSync` callers.\n\n### 3.4 Phase 4: Steady-State Watch\n\nAfter the initial list, the Reflector opens a Watch at the recorded `ResourceVersion`. Incoming `watch.Event` objects are converted to `Add`, `Update`, or `Delete` calls on the DeltaFIFO. The processLoop handles them identically to phase 3, except `isInInitialList=false`.\n\nWatch events carry the object's new ResourceVersion. The Reflector advances `lastSyncResourceVersion` on every event, ensuring the next watch or re-list starts from the correct point.\n\n### 3.5 Phase 5: Controller Reconciliation\n\nTypical controller code uses the informer-to-work-queue bridge:\n\n```go\ninformer.AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n    AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n        key, _ := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n        queue.Add(key)\n    },\n    UpdateFunc: func(_, new interface{}) { ... },\n    DeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) { ... },\n})\n```\n\nThe reconcile loop calls `queue.Get()` (blocks until an item is available), runs the reconcile function, then calls `queue.Done(key)`. If reconciliation fails, the controller calls `queue.AddRateLimited(key)` instead of `queue.Forget(key)`, which causes the item to be re-enqueued after an exponential back-off delay.\n\nThe key design insight: the controller reads the **current state from the informer's local cache** (via `lister.Pods(ns).Get(name)`), not from the API server. This eliminates per-reconcile API calls and provides a consistent snapshot.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Watch Gap / Missed Delete\n\nIf the watch connection drops and the Reflector misses a delete event before reconnecting, `DeltaFIFO.Replace()` detects the gap during re-list: the deleted object is in `KnownObjects` but not in the new list, so a `Deleted` delta with `DeletedFinalStateUnknown` is synthesized. Handlers receiving `OnDelete` with this type must be prepared for stale object state (`controller.go:261–263`).\n\n### 4.2 ResourceVersion Expiration\n\nEtcd compacts its event history. If the Reflector's `lastSyncResourceVersion` has been compacted away, the watch returns `HTTP 410 Gone`. `DefaultWatchErrorHandler` catches `isExpiredError` and lets `ListAndWatchWithContext` fall back to a full re-list from `ResourceVersion=\"\"`. This is transparent to consumers but causes a brief latency spike.\n\n### 4.3 Handler Backpressure\n\n`SharedInformer` comment at `shared_informer.go:136` explicitly warns: *\"A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of notifications to deliver.\"* Each `processorListener` has an unbounded ring buffer (`k8s.io/utils/buffer`). A slow handler causes memory to grow without bound. The intended pattern is to enqueue only a key into a work queue and do no non-trivial work in the handler.\n\n### 4.4 processLoop Serialization\n\nThe controller's `processLoop` (`controller.go:221`) calls `Pop()` sequentially. The comment at line 219 notes this explicitly: *\"TODO: Consider doing the processing in parallel.\"* For informers with high event rates, the single-threaded processLoop can become a bottleneck. `InOrderInformersBatchProcess` (beta, on by default as of v1.35) addresses this by batching multiple `Delta` values into a single `PopBatch` call, reducing lock overhead.\n\n### 4.5 Resync Cost\n\nResync delivers synthetic `OnUpdate` calls for every cached object, even if nothing changed. For informers caching tens of thousands of objects, this can produce a burst of reconcile work. Setting the resync period to zero (`0`) disables it entirely; when non-zero, the minimum enforced period is 1 second (`shared_informer.go:658`).\n\n### 4.6 Rate Limiting and the Two-Layer Model\n\n`client-go` applies rate limiting at two distinct levels:\n\n1. **RESTClient level** (`rest/config.go`): token-bucket on all outgoing HTTP requests (default 5 QPS / burst 10). This protects the API server from any single client.\n2. **Work queue level** (`util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go`): per-item exponential back-off composited with a global token bucket. This throttles *reconcile retries*, not raw API calls.\n\nThe two levels are independent. A controller that issues many API calls per reconcile can still exceed the RESTClient rate limit. Setting `QPS` and `Burst` in `rest.Config` must be calibrated to the expected reconcile frequency and the number of API calls per reconcile.\n\n### 4.7 Leader Election Guarantees\n\nThe leader election implementation (`tools/leaderelection/`) explicitly warns in its package comment that it *\"does not guarantee that only one client is acting as a leader\"* (no fencing token). Under severe clock skew or GC pauses, two instances can briefly believe they hold the lease. Applications that need strict mutual exclusion must implement external fencing (e.g., etcd's optimistic concurrency or resource-version checks).\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### 5.1 `TransformFunc` – Store Preprocessing\n\n`SharedInformer.SetTransform(TransformFunc)` (`shared_informer.go:232`) registers a function called on every object before it is stored in the local cache. The common use case is stripping fields that consume memory but are never needed by the controller (e.g., managed fields, last-applied annotation). Must be set before `Run()`.\n\n**Risk:** The transform is called in the processLoop goroutine under the DeltaFIFO lock. A slow or panicking transform blocks all event processing. Mutations made to the object in place will corrupt the cache and can cause subtle bugs; the function must return a new object or operate on a deep copy.\n\n### 5.2 `ResourceEventHandler` – Event Callbacks\n\n`AddEventHandler` / `AddEventHandlerWithOptions` registers callbacks for add/update/delete. Multiple handlers can be registered on a single informer. The `FilteringResourceEventHandler` adapter (`controller.go:339`) applies a predicate before dispatching.\n\n**Risk:** Handlers must not modify the objects they receive – the shared cache stores pointers, and mutations affect all other consumers of the same informer. The `MutationDetector` (`tools/cache/mutation_detector.go`) is a debug-mode facility that deep-copies objects and compares them periodically; enable it in tests by setting `KUBE_CACHE_MUTATION_DETECTOR=true`.\n\n### 5.3 Custom Indexers\n\n`AddIndexers(Indexers)` (`shared_informer.go:624`) can be called before the informer is started to add secondary indexes. This enables efficient lookups like \"all pods in namespace X with label Y\" via `ByIndex`.\n\n**Risk:** Index functions are called synchronously in the store's write path. An O(n) index function on large objects will amplify every event's processing cost. Indexes cannot be removed once added.\n\n### 5.4 `WrapTransport` – HTTP Middleware\n\n`rest/config.go:115` exposes `WrapTransport transport.WrapperFunc`, which layeres a `http.RoundTripper` on top of the base transport. This is the hook for custom authentication, tracing, metrics, and retry middleware.\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect middleware can break retries (by consuming the body), introduce request ordering dependencies, or silently swallow errors. Middleware added via `WrapTransport` runs before the client's rate limiter.\n\n### 5.5 `ListerWatcher` – Custom Data Sources\n\nThe `ListerWatcher` interface (`tools/cache/listwatch.go:38,66`) can be implemented to back an informer from any list/watch source, not just the API server. This is how `controller-runtime`'s dynamic informers and webhook-backed caches are built.\n\n**Risk:** The Reflector makes assumptions about the `ResourceVersion` semantics of returned objects. Custom implementations that do not honor monotonically increasing resource versions will cause the Reflector to loop in re-list or fail to detect updates.\n\n### 5.6 Feature Gates – Runtime Behavioral Switches\n\n`features/features.go` exposes `ReplaceFeatureGates(Gates)` for embedding binaries to plug in their own feature gate implementation (e.g., kube-controller-manager's component-base gate). This allows the same client-go code path to participate in the cluster's global feature flag system.\n\n**Risk:** `ReplaceFeatureGates` must be called before any informer is constructed. If called after feature gates have been read (e.g., after the first informer starts), a warning is emitted and behavior may be inconsistent (`features.go:129`).\n\n### 5.7 Custom Rate Limiters\n\nThe `TypedRateLimiter` interface is open for extension. A custom limiter can implement priority-based scheduling (e.g., process CRD updates before status updates) or integrate with an external admission controller's token service.\n\n**Risk:** Returning a very large `When()` value from a rate limiter causes items to stall in the delaying queue's min-heap indefinitely. Failing to call `Forget(item)` after success leaks per-item failure counters, causing ever-increasing delays for future occurrences of the same key.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Memory Footprint\n\nEach informer holds an in-memory copy of every object of its type. For high-cardinality resources (Pods, Endpoints, EndpointSlices), this is the dominant memory consumer in controllers. Mitigation options:\n\n- **`TransformFunc`**: strip unused fields before storage. Dropping `metadata.managedFields` and `metadata.annotations[\"kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration\"]` can halve the per-object footprint.\n- **Field/Label selectors via `WithTweakListOptions`** (`factory.go:87`): narrow the informer's scope at the API server, reducing the number of objects transferred and cached.\n- **`WithNamespace`** (`factory.go:95`): restrict to a single namespace when cross-namespace visibility is not needed.\n\n### 6.2 API Server Connection Count\n\nEach distinct `SharedIndexInformer` maintains one long-lived watch connection to the API server. A factory with N resource types opens N watch connections. At scale (many controllers, many resource types), this can exhaust API server connection limits. Prefer the `SharedInformerFactory` over constructing informers directly; it enforces one informer per type per factory instance.\n\n### 6.3 Startup Latency and `HasSynced`\n\nControllers must wait for `WaitForCacheSync` before processing work-queue items. This blocks until every informer has completed its initial list. For clusters with millions of objects, the initial list is paginated and can take 10–30 seconds. The `WatchListClient` feature gate (`known_features.go:89`, beta default-on since v1.35) replaces the initial list with a streaming watch, which can significantly reduce startup latency on high-object-count clusters.\n\n### 6.4 Resync Tuning\n\nSetting a non-zero `defaultResync` on the factory causes all informers to periodically re-deliver every cached object as `OnUpdate` events. If 50,000 Pods exist and the resync period is 30 seconds, controllers receive 50,000/30 ≈ 1,667 reconcile triggers per second at steady state just from resyncs, even with no actual changes. For controllers whose reconciliation is purely event-driven, set resync to 0.\n\n### 6.5 Work Queue Observability\n\nNamed queues emit Prometheus metrics (queue depth, add rate, processing latency, unfinished work) via the `MetricsProvider` interface (`util/workqueue/metrics.go`). Unnamed queues (constructed via `workqueue.New()` without a name) do not emit metrics. Always name production queues via `TypedQueueConfig.Name`.\n\nThe `unfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod` (500 ms by default) drives a goroutine that periodically updates the `workqueue_unfinished_work_seconds` gauge. A growing unfinished-work metric indicates a reconcile loop that is taking too long or is deadlocked.\n\n### 6.6 CBOR Wire Format\n\n`features/known_features.go:49-60` shows `ClientsAllowCBOR` and `ClientsPreferCBOR` (alpha as of v1.32). When enabled, `client-go` negotiates CBOR encoding with the API server instead of JSON. CBOR is more compact and faster to decode for large objects. These gates are off by default; operators should not enable them in production until the API server's CBOR support stabilizes.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File Map\n\nThe following are the most important files for understanding `client-go`'s behavior, as used in this analysis:\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/client-go/\n├── features/\n│   ├── features.go              # FeatureGates interface, ReplaceFeatureGates, envvar implementation\n│   └── known_features.go        # All client-go feature gate constants and default values\n├── informers/\n│   └── factory.go               # SharedInformerFactory: registry, Start, WaitForCacheSync, InformerFor\n├── rest/\n│   ├── client.go                # RESTClient: base URL, rate limiter, verb factories\n│   ├── config.go                # Config struct: credentials, QPS, Burst, WrapTransport, Timeout\n│   ├── request.go               # Request: fluent builder, Do, Watch, Stream execution\n│   └── with_retry.go            # WithRetry interface; per-request retry/backoff policy\n├── tools/cache/\n│   ├── controller.go            # Controller interface; processLoop; ResourceEventHandler types;\n│   │                            # FilteringResourceEventHandler; LeaseDuration/RenewDeadline/RetryPeriod semantics\n└── util/workqueue/\n    ├── default_rate_limiters.go # DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter; ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter;\n    │                            # BucketRateLimiter; MaxOfRateLimiter\n    ├── delaying_queue.go        # TypedDelayingInterface; AddAfter; min-heap scheduler\n    ├── queue.go                 # Typed[T]: dirty/processing/queue triset; Add/Get/Done/ShutDown\n    └── rate_limiting_queue.go   # TypedRateLimitingInterface; Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n`client-go` is the official Go client library for the Kubernetes API. It sits at the intersection of every controller, operator, and internal control-plane component in the Kubernetes ecosystem. Its role is to:\n\n- Provide authenticated, rate-limited, retry-capable HTTP access to the kube-apiserver's REST API.\n- Abstract the list/watch protocol into an eventually-consistent local cache (the *informer* machinery).\n- Expose a work-queue primitive that decouples event receipt from reconciliation, enabling a well-known controller pattern.\n- Offer ancillary facilities: leader election, port forwarding, remote command execution, and structured metrics.\n\n**Upstream dependencies.** `client-go` depends on `k8s.io/apimachinery` for API object types, serializers, and the watch event protocol, and on `k8s.io/api` for the concrete Kubernetes object types. It imports `k8s.io/utils` for clock abstraction (test seam), exponential backoff, and buffer utilities.\n\n**Downstream consumers.** Every Kubernetes built-in controller (scheduler, node-controller, endpoint-slice controller, etc.) uses `client-go`. Third-party operators and `controller-runtime`-based projects sit on top of the same informer/work-queue contract. The API server itself uses `client-go` for its own internal clients when it acts as a consumer (e.g. admission webhooks with client access).\n\n**Staging location.** The authoritative source lives under `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/` in the main Kubernetes repository and is published as a standalone module. All references in this document use the staging path.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Boundaries\n\nThe library divides cleanly into four layers:\n\n### 2.1 REST Layer (`rest/`)\n\nThe REST layer is the raw transport. Key files:\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `rest/config.go` | `Config` struct – holds credentials, QPS, burst, TLS, `WrapTransport` |\n| `rest/client.go` | `RESTClient` – root URL, rate limiter, content negotiation, `http.Client` |\n| `rest/request.go` | `Request` – fluent builder for a single HTTP call |\n| `rest/with_retry.go` | `WithRetry` interface – per-request retry policy |\n\n`RESTClient` (`rest/client.go:86`) holds an `http.Client`, a root URL, and a `flowcontrol.RateLimiter`. It provides verb-oriented factory methods (`Get()`, `Post()`, `Verb(v)`) that return a `*Request`. The `Request` object accumulates the resource path, query parameters, body, and headers, then executes the call via `Do(ctx)` or opens a watch stream via `Watch(ctx)`.\n\n`rest/config.go` exposes `DefaultQPS = 5.0` and `DefaultBurst = 10` as the built-in rate-limit knobs. QPS / Burst together feed a token-bucket rate limiter whose delay is logged when it exceeds `longThrottleLatency = 50ms` (`rest/request.go:57–61`).\n\n`rest/with_retry.go` defines `WithRetry`, which governs whether a failed request is retried. The default implementation backs off on 429 and 5xx responses and rewinds the request body before retrying.\n\n### 2.2 Informer Machinery (`tools/cache/`)\n\nThis is the heart of the controller pattern. It comprises five cooperating types:\n\n#### Reflector (`tools/cache/reflector.go`)\n\nThe `Reflector` owns the connection to the API server for a single resource type. It is instantiated with a `ListerWatcher` and a target `ReflectorStore`, and runs a continuous `ListAndWatchWithContext` loop (`reflector.go:408`):\n\n1. On startup (or after a watch failure), it issues a **List** call (paginated via `tools/pager`) to populate the store with an initial snapshot, recording the resulting `ResourceVersion`.\n2. If the `WatchListClient` feature gate is enabled (beta as of v1.35, `features/known_features.go:89`), it can instead open a streaming **WatchList** request that returns items as a watch stream, avoiding the full list-then-watch round trip.\n3. It then opens a `Watch` call from that `ResourceVersion`, consuming `watch.Event` objects and routing them to the store via `store.Add`, `store.Update`, `store.Delete`, or `store.Replace`.\n4. On watch termination it calls `watchErrorHandler` and restarts via an exponential back-off manager seeded at 800 ms, capped at 30 s (`reflector.go:282`).\n5. Concurrently, `startResync` fires the store's `Resync()` at the configured period, triggering re-delivery of Sync deltas for all known objects.\n\nThe watch timeout is randomized in `[minWatchTimeout, 2*minWatchTimeout]` (default 5–10 min) to spread load across many watchers (`reflector.go:526–536`). Bookmarks (`AllowWatchBookmarks: true`) are always requested to advance `lastSyncResourceVersion` without requiring a full re-list.\n\n#### DeltaFIFO / RealFIFO (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`, `tools/cache/the_real_fifo.go`)\n\nThe `DeltaFIFO` is the staging queue between the Reflector (producer) and the controller's `processLoop` (consumer). Its defining characteristic is that it accumulates **change history** (Deltas) keyed by object identity, not just the latest state.\n\nA Delta has a type (`Added`, `Updated`, `Deleted`, `Replaced`, `Sync`) and an object. When the same object key is enqueued multiple times before the consumer pops it, the accumulator grows:\n\n```\nkey \"default/pod-a\" → [Delta{Sync, pod-a-v1}, Delta{Updated, pod-a-v2}]\n```\n\n`Pop()` dequeues an entire `Deltas` slice under lock and calls the `ProcessFunc` while still holding it. This design means the controller sees every intermediate state, never skips a change, and can detect the difference between a net-new object and an update.\n\nWhen the `InOrderInformers` feature gate is enabled (beta, on by default since v1.33 – `known_features.go:66`), the queue is a `RealFIFO` instead of `DeltaFIFO`. `RealFIFO` delivers events in strict arrival order and, when `UnlockWhileProcessingFIFO` is also enabled, releases the queue lock during `ProcessFunc` execution to allow concurrent producers to continue adding events.\n\nThe `KnownObjects` reference back to the downstream `Store` is critical: during a `Replace()` call (initial list or re-list), `DeltaFIFO` computes the symmetric difference between the listed keys and `KnownObjects.ListKeys()` to synthesize `Deleted` deltas for any objects that have vanished.\n\n#### Store / Indexer (`tools/cache/store.go`, `tools/cache/index.go`, `tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`)\n\nThe `Store` interface (`store.go:41`) is a keyed map of live objects with `Add`, `Update`, `Delete`, `List`, `Get`, `GetByKey`, `Replace`, and `Resync` methods. The concrete implementation is `cache` (lowercase, unexported), which wraps a `ThreadSafeStore`.\n\n`ThreadSafeStore` (`thread_safe_store.go:43`) couples a `sync.RWMutex`-protected object map with a `storeIndex` – the secondary index structure. An `Indexer` (`index.go:35`) extends `Store` with `Index`, `ByIndex`, `IndexKeys`, and `ListIndexFuncValues`. Callers register `IndexFunc` functions (returning a slice of string keys) under named indexes; the `NamespaceIndex` / `MetaNamespaceIndexFunc` pair is the canonical example, mapping objects to their namespace.\n\nLookups like `informer.GetIndexer().ByIndex(\"namespace\", \"kube-system\")` are O(1) set lookups, not linear scans – the store maintains an inverted index (map[indexedValue]set[storageKey]).\n\n#### sharedIndexInformer (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`)\n\n`sharedIndexInformer` (`shared_informer.go:420`) is the user-facing type. It owns three sub-components:\n\n1. **`indexer Indexer`** – the live object cache, described above.\n2. **`controller Controller`** – a low-level controller (`tools/cache/controller.go:114`) that runs the Reflector and the processLoop.\n3. **`processor *sharedProcessor`** – fan-out relay to N registered event handlers.\n\nThe controller's `ProcessFunc` is `sharedIndexInformer.HandleDeltas`, which (under a `blockDeltas` mutex) applies each delta to `indexer` then notifies the `sharedProcessor`. The mutex prevents a race between late-joining handlers (which replay the existing cache) and live delta processing.\n\n`sharedProcessor` (`shared_informer.go:803`) holds a map of `*processorListener` values. Each listener has two goroutines: `pop` drains a channel and transfers notifications to a ring-buffer (`k8s.io/utils/buffer`), and `run` drains the buffer and calls the user's `ResourceEventHandler`. This two-goroutine design decouples a slow handler from stalling the distribution path. Resync-only notifications are filtered per-listener based on each listener's `resyncPeriod`, allowing different handlers to request different resync cadences from the same underlying informer connection.\n\n#### SharedInformerFactory (`informers/factory.go`)\n\n`sharedInformerFactory` (`factory.go:57`) is a registry of one `SharedIndexInformer` per `reflect.Type`. When code calls `factory.Core().V1().Pods().Informer()`, the factory lazily constructs the informer (if absent), stores it keyed by `reflect.TypeOf(&v1.Pod{})`, and returns the shared instance. All callers that request the same type share a single Reflector and a single store, so one watch connection services all controllers interested in Pods.\n\n`factory.Start(stopCh)` (`factory.go:144`) iterates the map and starts each not-yet-started informer in its own goroutine. `WaitForCacheSync` polls `informer.HasSynced()` at 100 ms intervals until all informers report that the initial list has been processed.\n\n### 2.3 Work Queue (`util/workqueue/`)\n\nThe work queue decouples informer event delivery from the reconciliation loop. Key files:\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `util/workqueue/queue.go` | Base `Typed[T]` queue with deduplication |\n| `util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go` | Adds `AddAfter(item, delay)` |\n| `util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go` | Adds `AddRateLimited`, `Forget`, `NumRequeues` |\n| `util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go` | Built-in rate limiter implementations |\n\n`Typed[T]` (`queue.go:190`) maintains three data structures under a single mutex:\n\n- **`queue Queue[T]`** – ordered FIFO of items to be processed (no duplicates at any moment).\n- **`dirty sets.Set[T]`** – the union of queued and currently-processing items that are pending.\n- **`processing sets.Set[T]`** – items currently held by a `Get()` caller.\n\n`Add(item)` inserts into `dirty`. If the item is already in `processing`, it does not enqueue it again – instead the item remains in `dirty` and is re-enqueued when `Done(item)` is called. This guarantees that if an object changes while it is being reconciled, reconciliation runs again, but never more than once per pending change.\n\n`TypedRateLimitingInterface` (`rate_limiting_queue.go:27`) wraps a `TypedDelayingInterface` (which uses a min-heap for delayed delivery) and delegates rate decisions to a `TypedRateLimiter`. The **default rate limiter** (`default_rate_limiters.go:50`) composites two limiters via `MaxOfRateLimiter`:\n\n- `ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter`: per-item back-off starting at 5 ms, doubling on each failure, capped at 1000 s.\n- `BucketRateLimiter`: token-bucket at 10 QPS / burst 100, global across all items.\n\nThe composite means an item that fails repeatedly backs off exponentially (protecting the API server from hammering), while the global bucket prevents a large burst of distinct keys from flooding it.\n\n### 2.4 Ancillary Tools\n\n- **`tools/leaderelection/`** – distributed leader election using Kubernetes `Lease`, `ConfigMap`, or `Endpoints` objects as a lock. Tolerant of arbitrary clock skew; tunable via `LeaseDuration`, `RenewDeadline`, and `RetryPeriod` (`leaderelection.go:76–101`). Provides `OnStartedLeading`, `OnStoppedLeading`, and `OnNewLeader` callbacks.\n- **`tools/clientcmd/`** – kubeconfig parsing, merging, and REST config construction from KUBECONFIG files or in-cluster service account tokens.\n- **`transport/`** – TLS configuration, exec-based credential plugins, and `WrapperFunc` chain for pluggable authentication middleware.\n- **`util/flowcontrol/`** – token-bucket `RateLimiter` used directly by `RESTClient`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\nThis section traces the full path from a Kubernetes object change to a controller reconciling it.\n\n### 3.1 Phase 1: Startup\n\n```\ncontroller binary\n  └── NewSharedInformerFactory(client, resyncPeriod)   [informers/factory.go:112]\n       └── factory.Core().V1().Pods().Informer()\n            └── factory.InformerFor(&v1.Pod{}, newPodInformer)  [factory.go:200]\n                 └── NewSharedIndexInformerWithOptions(lw, &v1.Pod{}, opts) [shared_informer.go:303]\n                      └── sharedIndexInformer{\n                            indexer:    NewIndexer(MetaNamespaceKeyFunc, opts.Indexers),\n                            processor:  &sharedProcessor{},\n                            listerWatcher: lw,\n                          }\n```\n\nThe factory's `InformerFor` is idempotent – calling it twice with the same type returns the same instance.\n\n### 3.2 Phase 2: Running\n\n`factory.Start(stopCh)` spawns one goroutine per informer type: `go informer.Run(stopCh)`.\n\nInside `sharedIndexInformer.RunWithContext` (`shared_informer.go:537`):\n\n1. A `DeltaFIFO` (or `RealFIFO` if `InOrderInformers` is enabled) is created with `s.indexer` as `KnownObjects`.\n2. A `Config` is built connecting the FIFO to `HandleDeltas` as the `ProcessFunc`.\n3. A `controller` is created and run: it spawns a `Reflector.RunWithContext` goroutine and then enters `processLoop`.\n4. The `sharedProcessor.run` goroutine starts all listener goroutine pairs.\n\n### 3.3 Phase 3: Initial List\n\n`Reflector.ListAndWatchWithContext` (`reflector.go:408`) calls `r.list(ctx)`, which:\n\n1. Issues a paginated LIST (via `tools/pager`) at `ResourceVersion=\"\"` (consistent read from etcd).\n2. Calls `r.store.Replace(items, resourceVersion)` on the DeltaFIFO.\n3. `DeltaFIFO.Replace` computes deletion deltas for objects in `KnownObjects` not in the list, then enqueues `Replaced` deltas for all listed objects.\n\n`processLoop` pops each `Deltas` slice and calls `HandleDeltas`, which in turn calls `processDeltas` (`controller.go:581`). For each delta of type `Replaced`/`Added`:\n\n- If the object exists in `indexer`: call `indexer.Update(obj)` then `handler.OnUpdate(old, obj)`.\n- Otherwise: call `indexer.Add(obj)` then `handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList=true)`.\n\n`sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd` calls `processor.distribute(addNotification{...}, false)`, which fans out to every `processorListener.add(...)`. Each listener's `pop` goroutine buffers the notification; `run` drains the buffer and calls the user's `ResourceEventHandler.OnAdd`.\n\nAfter all `Replace` deltas are processed, `controller.HasSynced()` returns `true`, unblocking any `WaitForCacheSync` callers.\n\n### 3.4 Phase 4: Steady-State Watch\n\nAfter the initial list, the Reflector opens a Watch at the recorded `ResourceVersion`. Incoming `watch.Event` objects are converted to `Add`, `Update`, or `Delete` calls on the DeltaFIFO. The processLoop handles them identically to phase 3, except `isInInitialList=false`.\n\nWatch events carry the object's new ResourceVersion. The Reflector advances `lastSyncResourceVersion` on every event, ensuring the next watch or re-list starts from the correct point.\n\n### 3.5 Phase 5: Controller Reconciliation\n\nTypical controller code uses the informer-to-work-queue bridge:\n\n```go\ninformer.AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n    AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n        key, _ := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n        queue.Add(key)\n    },\n    UpdateFunc: func(_, new interface{}) { ... },\n    DeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) { ... },\n})\n```\n\nThe reconcile loop calls `queue.Get()` (blocks until an item is available), runs the reconcile function, then calls `queue.Done(key)`. If reconciliation fails, the controller calls `queue.AddRateLimited(key)` instead of `queue.Forget(key)`, which causes the item to be re-enqueued after an exponential back-off delay.\n\nThe key design insight: the controller reads the **current state from the informer's local cache** (via `lister.Pods(ns).Get(name)`), not from the API server. This eliminates per-reconcile API calls and provides a consistent snapshot.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Watch Gap / Missed Delete\n\nIf the watch connection drops and the Reflector misses a delete event before reconnecting, `DeltaFIFO.Replace()` detects the gap during re-list: the deleted object is in `KnownObjects` but not in the new list, so a `Deleted` delta with `DeletedFinalStateUnknown` is synthesized. Handlers receiving `OnDelete` with this type must be prepared for stale object state (`controller.go:261–263`).\n\n### 4.2 ResourceVersion Expiration\n\nEtcd compacts its event history. If the Reflector's `lastSyncResourceVersion` has been compacted away, the watch returns `HTTP 410 Gone`. `DefaultWatchErrorHandler` catches `isExpiredError` and lets `ListAndWatchWithContext` fall back to a full re-list from `ResourceVersion=\"\"`. This is transparent to consumers but causes a brief latency spike.\n\n### 4.3 Handler Backpressure\n\n`SharedInformer` comment at `shared_informer.go:136` explicitly warns: *\"A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of notifications to deliver.\"* Each `processorListener` has an unbounded ring buffer (`k8s.io/utils/buffer`). A slow handler causes memory to grow without bound. The intended pattern is to enqueue only a key into a work queue and do no non-trivial work in the handler.\n\n### 4.4 processLoop Serialization\n\nThe controller's `processLoop` (`controller.go:221`) calls `Pop()` sequentially. The comment at line 219 notes this explicitly: *\"TODO: Consider doing the processing in parallel.\"* For informers with high event rates, the single-threaded processLoop can become a bottleneck. `InOrderInformersBatchProcess` (beta, on by default as of v1.35) addresses this by batching multiple `Delta` values into a single `PopBatch` call, reducing lock overhead.\n\n### 4.5 Resync Cost\n\nResync delivers synthetic `OnUpdate` calls for every cached object, even if nothing changed. For informers caching tens of thousands of objects, this can produce a burst of reconcile work. Setting the resync period to zero (`0`) disables it entirely; when non-zero, the minimum enforced period is 1 second (`shared_informer.go:658`).\n\n### 4.6 Rate Limiting and the Two-Layer Model\n\n`client-go` applies rate limiting at two distinct levels:\n\n1. **RESTClient level** (`rest/config.go`): token-bucket on all outgoing HTTP requests (default 5 QPS / burst 10). This protects the API server from any single client.\n2. **Work queue level** (`util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go`): per-item exponential back-off composited with a global token bucket. This throttles *reconcile retries*, not raw API calls.\n\nThe two levels are independent. A controller that issues many API calls per reconcile can still exceed the RESTClient rate limit. Setting `QPS` and `Burst` in `rest.Config` must be calibrated to the expected reconcile frequency and the number of API calls per reconcile.\n\n### 4.7 Leader Election Guarantees\n\nThe leader election implementation (`tools/leaderelection/`) explicitly warns in its package comment that it *\"does not guarantee that only one client is acting as a leader\"* (no fencing token). Under severe clock skew or GC pauses, two instances can briefly believe they hold the lease. Applications that need strict mutual exclusion must implement external fencing (e.g., etcd's optimistic concurrency or resource-version checks).\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### 5.1 `TransformFunc` – Store Preprocessing\n\n`SharedInformer.SetTransform(TransformFunc)` (`shared_informer.go:232`) registers a function called on every object before it is stored in the local cache. The common use case is stripping fields that consume memory but are never needed by the controller (e.g., managed fields, last-applied annotation). Must be set before `Run()`.\n\n**Risk:** The transform is called in the processLoop goroutine under the DeltaFIFO lock. A slow or panicking transform blocks all event processing. Mutations made to the object in place will corrupt the cache and can cause subtle bugs; the function must return a new object or operate on a deep copy.\n\n### 5.2 `ResourceEventHandler` – Event Callbacks\n\n`AddEventHandler` / `AddEventHandlerWithOptions` registers callbacks for add/update/delete. Multiple handlers can be registered on a single informer. The `FilteringResourceEventHandler` adapter (`controller.go:339`) applies a predicate before dispatching.\n\n**Risk:** Handlers must not modify the objects they receive – the shared cache stores pointers, and mutations affect all other consumers of the same informer. The `MutationDetector` (`tools/cache/mutation_detector.go`) is a debug-mode facility that deep-copies objects and compares them periodically; enable it in tests by setting `KUBE_CACHE_MUTATION_DETECTOR=true`.\n\n### 5.3 Custom Indexers\n\n`AddIndexers(Indexers)` (`shared_informer.go:624`) can be called before the informer is started to add secondary indexes. This enables efficient lookups like \"all pods in namespace X with label Y\" via `ByIndex`.\n\n**Risk:** Index functions are called synchronously in the store's write path. An O(n) index function on large objects will amplify every event's processing cost. Indexes cannot be removed once added.\n\n### 5.4 `WrapTransport` – HTTP Middleware\n\n`rest/config.go:115` exposes `WrapTransport transport.WrapperFunc`, which layeres a `http.RoundTripper` on top of the base transport. This is the hook for custom authentication, tracing, metrics, and retry middleware.\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect middleware can break retries (by consuming the body), introduce request ordering dependencies, or silently swallow errors. Middleware added via `WrapTransport` runs before the client's rate limiter.\n\n### 5.5 `ListerWatcher` – Custom Data Sources\n\nThe `ListerWatcher` interface (`tools/cache/listwatch.go:38,66`) can be implemented to back an informer from any list/watch source, not just the API server. This is how `controller-runtime`'s dynamic informers and webhook-backed caches are built.\n\n**Risk:** The Reflector makes assumptions about the `ResourceVersion` semantics of returned objects. Custom implementations that do not honor monotonically increasing resource versions will cause the Reflector to loop in re-list or fail to detect updates.\n\n### 5.6 Feature Gates – Runtime Behavioral Switches\n\n`features/features.go` exposes `ReplaceFeatureGates(Gates)` for embedding binaries to plug in their own feature gate implementation (e.g., kube-controller-manager's component-base gate). This allows the same client-go code path to participate in the cluster's global feature flag system.\n\n**Risk:** `ReplaceFeatureGates` must be called before any informer is constructed. If called after feature gates have been read (e.g., after the first informer starts), a warning is emitted and behavior may be inconsistent (`features.go:129`).\n\n### 5.7 Custom Rate Limiters\n\nThe `TypedRateLimiter` interface is open for extension. A custom limiter can implement priority-based scheduling (e.g., process CRD updates before status updates) or integrate with an external admission controller's token service.\n\n**Risk:** Returning a very large `When()` value from a rate limiter causes items to stall in the delaying queue's min-heap indefinitely. Failing to call `Forget(item)` after success leaks per-item failure counters, causing ever-increasing delays for future occurrences of the same key.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Memory Footprint\n\nEach informer holds an in-memory copy of every object of its type. For high-cardinality resources (Pods, Endpoints, EndpointSlices), this is the dominant memory consumer in controllers. Mitigation options:\n\n- **`TransformFunc`**: strip unused fields before storage. Dropping `metadata.managedFields` and `metadata.annotations[\"kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration\"]` can halve the per-object footprint.\n- **Field/Label selectors via `WithTweakListOptions`** (`factory.go:87`): narrow the informer's scope at the API server, reducing the number of objects transferred and cached.\n- **`WithNamespace`** (`factory.go:95`): restrict to a single namespace when cross-namespace visibility is not needed.\n\n### 6.2 API Server Connection Count\n\nEach distinct `SharedIndexInformer` maintains one long-lived watch connection to the API server. A factory with N resource types opens N watch connections. At scale (many controllers, many resource types), this can exhaust API server connection limits. Prefer the `SharedInformerFactory` over constructing informers directly; it enforces one informer per type per factory instance.\n\n### 6.3 Startup Latency and `HasSynced`\n\nControllers must wait for `WaitForCacheSync` before processing work-queue items. This blocks until every informer has completed its initial list. For clusters with millions of objects, the initial list is paginated and can take 10–30 seconds. The `WatchListClient` feature gate (`known_features.go:89`, beta default-on since v1.35) replaces the initial list with a streaming watch, which can significantly reduce startup latency on high-object-count clusters.\n\n### 6.4 Resync Tuning\n\nSetting a non-zero `defaultResync` on the factory causes all informers to periodically re-deliver every cached object as `OnUpdate` events. If 50,000 Pods exist and the resync period is 30 seconds, controllers receive 50,000/30 ≈ 1,667 reconcile triggers per second at steady state just from resyncs, even with no actual changes. For controllers whose reconciliation is purely event-driven, set resync to 0.\n\n### 6.5 Work Queue Observability\n\nNamed queues emit Prometheus metrics (queue depth, add rate, processing latency, unfinished work) via the `MetricsProvider` interface (`util/workqueue/metrics.go`). Unnamed queues (constructed via `workqueue.New()` without a name) do not emit metrics. Always name production queues via `TypedQueueConfig.Name`.\n\nThe `unfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod` (500 ms by default) drives a goroutine that periodically updates the `workqueue_unfinished_work_seconds` gauge. A growing unfinished-work metric indicates a reconcile loop that is taking too long or is deadlocked.\n\n### 6.6 CBOR Wire Format\n\n`features/known_features.go:49-60` shows `ClientsAllowCBOR` and `ClientsPreferCBOR` (alpha as of v1.32). When enabled, `client-go` negotiates CBOR encoding with the API server instead of JSON. CBOR is more compact and faster to decode for large objects. These gates are off by default; operators should not enable them in production until the API server's CBOR support stabilizes.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File Map\n\nThe following are the most important files for understanding `client-go`'s behavior, as used in this analysis:\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/client-go/\n├── features/\n│   ├── features.go              # FeatureGates interface, ReplaceFeatureGates, envvar implementation\n│   └── known_features.go        # All client-go feature gate constants and default values\n├── informers/\n│   └── factory.go               # SharedInformerFactory: registry, Start, WaitForCacheSync, InformerFor\n├── rest/\n│   ├── client.go                # RESTClient: base URL, rate limiter, verb factories\n│   ├── config.go                # Config struct: credentials, QPS, Burst, WrapTransport, Timeout\n│   ├── request.go               # Request: fluent builder, Do, Watch, Stream execution\n│   └── with_retry.go            # WithRetry interface; per-request retry/backoff policy\n├── tools/cache/\n│   ├── controller.go            # Controller interface; processLoop; ResourceEventHandler types;\n│   │                            # FilteringResourceEventHandler; processDeltas; processDeltasInBatch\n│   ├── delta_fifo.go            # DeltaFIFO: accumulator queue; Replace; Resync; KnownObjects\n│   ├── index.go                 # Indexer interface; IndexFunc; NamespaceIndex constant\n│   ├── listwatch.go             # ListerWatcher, ListerWatcherWithContext interfaces\n│   ├── reflector.go             # Reflector: ListAndWatchWithContext; LeaseDuration/RenewDeadline/RetryPeriod semantics\n└── util/workqueue/\n    ├── default_rate_limiters.go # DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter; ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter;\n    │                            # BucketRateLimiter; MaxOfRateLimiter\n    ├── delaying_queue.go        # TypedDelayingInterface; AddAfter; min-heap scheduler\n    ├── queue.go                 # Typed[T]: dirty/processing/queue triset; Add/Get/Done/ShutDown\n    └── rate_limiting_queue.go   # TypedRateLimitingInterface;
